title": "Adobo sauce recipe",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Adobo sauce recipe, Cooking with chillies\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chicken #vinegar #balsamicvinegar #onions #bayleaf #adobosaucerecipe #soysauce #ricevinegar #bones #blackpeppercorns #browning \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Apparently adobo sauce is one of the first dish that Filipinos learn to cook\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1747\n|PortionCalories = 436\n|DatePublished=2nd January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 40 minutes\n|PrepTime = 5 minutes\n|CookTime = 35 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Chicken adobo.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Very nice with chicken wings</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.7</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Made this with Danyu Chinkiang vinegar and it was perfect.</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]]</span></span>\n}}\nApparently [[adobo sauce]] is one of the first dish that Filipinos learn to cook.\n\nYou could also use [[pork spare ribs]] for this dish.\n\nThe traditional Filipino dish uses suka vinegar, but as that's not likely to be available in Europe, we have substituted it with [[balsamic vinegar]]. [[Rice vinegar|Black rice vinegar]] is also a very good substitute.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 kg Selection of [[chicken]] legs and thighs, with [[bones]] and skin, for four people\n| 8 teaspoons [[balsamic vinegar]]\n| 8 teaspoons [[soy sauce]]\n| 1 finely sliced [[onion]]\n| 4 [[garlic cloves, peeled and crushed]]\n| 1 whole [[bay leaf]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[black peppercorns]], partially crushed in a mortal and pestle\n| [[Vegetable oil]] for [[frying]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Sear the [[chicken]] in a hot pan for about 4 minutes, [[browning]]  the legs and thighs. Leave them in the pan\n| Turn down the heat and add some [[oil]], add the [[onions]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] and soften the [[onions]]. When they are translucent, add the [[vinegar]]\n| Let the [[vinegar]] almost [[boil]] away before you stir the pan\n| Once the [[vinegar]] has reduced, add in the [[soy sauce]], [[bay leaf]] and [[pepper]].\n| Cook until the [[sauce]] has reduced more and the [[chicken]] is properly cooked. Real adobo should be on the dry side\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe with [[plain boiled rice]]\n==See also==\n* [[Chilli sauce|Many other chilli sauce recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Marinades dressings and butters]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Spices|Adobo]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #vinegar #balsamicvinegar #onions #bayleaf #adobosaucerecipe #soysauce #ricevinegar #bones #blackpeppercorns #browning </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

|TotalTime = 12 hours 45 minutes\n |PrepTime = 12 hours 5 minutes\n |CookTime = 40 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Ajam kelapa (Chicken in spicy coconut sauce) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Spicey!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Nice and galicy</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The&nbsp;Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\nThis is an easy [[Chicken|chicken]] recipe from Malaya.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 kg [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces (bone in) or 500-600 g (boneless)\n| 1&frac12; teaspoons [[Turmeric|turmeric]]\n| [[Salt]]\n| 1&frac12; tablespoons [[Fresh ginger|fresh ginger]] root, peeled\n| 2 medium [[Onions|onions]], roughly chopped\n| 4 bulbs [[Garlic|garlic]], or to taste, peeled\n| 1 tablespoon [[Sambal#Sambal Ulek (Oelek)|sambal ulek]] or to taste\n| 30 ml water\n| 60 ml [[Peanut oil|peanut oil]]\n| 500 ml thick [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| 2 [[Curry leaves|curry leaves]]\n| 1 [[Spring onion|spring onion]], finely chopped\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* [[Marinate]] the [[Chicken|chicken]] (see below).\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Wash and dry the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces.\n| Rub the [[Turmeric|turmeric]] with a little [[Salt|salt]] into the [[Chicken|chicken]] and place in a bowl.\n| Using a [[Food processor|food processor]] or [[Blender|blender]], pur\u00e9e the [[Ginger|ginger]], [[Onions|onions]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Sambal#Sambal Ulek (Oelek)|sambal ulek]] and water.\n| Pour over the [[Chicken|chicken]], mix well and [[Marinate|marinate]] for several hours or overnight.\n| Remove the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces from the [[Marinade|marinade]] (remove as much marinade as possible) and reserve.\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a [[Wok|wok]] to a moderate heat and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] the [[Marinade|marinade]] for a couple of minutes.\n| Add the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] until they are golden [[Brown|brown]] (about 10 minutes).\n| Add the [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]], [[Sugar|sugar]] and [[Curry leaves|curry leaves]].\n| Stir, [[Salt|salt]] to taste and [[Simmer|simmer]], partially covered until the [[Chicken|chicken]] is cooked.\n| Serve garnished with the chopped [[Spring onion|spring onion]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Nasi sayur]].\n===Variations===\nIf using boneless [[Chicken|chicken]], you can cut it into smaller chunks, but you will need to reduce the cooking time accordingly.\n\nTry it with other [[Poultry|poultry]] or [[Game|game]] birds.\n==See also==\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Chicken in spicy coconut sauce]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes|Chicken in spicy coconut sauce]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Chicken                         "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Almond chicken, Meat recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chicken #almondchicken #butter #onions #almonds #cornflour #lemon #parsley #onion #garlic #chervil \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Another nice way to cook chicken breasts. White wine with white meat\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1366\n|PortionCalories = 341\n|DatePublished=24th October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 50 minutes\n|PrepTime = 15 minutes\n|CookTime = 35 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Almond chicken recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Fabulous!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Cannot stop making this!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\nAnother nice way to cook [[chicken]] breasts.  White wine with with white meat.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 4 [[chicken]] breasts, [[bones]] and skin removed\n| 40 g (1 &frac12; oz) [[butter]]\n| Juice from &frac12; a [[lemon]]\n| Chopped zest from &frac14; of a [[lemon]]\n| 40 g (1 &frac12; oz) [[almond]] flakes or halves, chopped and toasted, browned but NOT burnt\n| 1 [[garlic clove, crushed]]\n| 1 [[onion]], sliced finely\n| 1 bell pepper (or a coloured mix of bell peppers), chopped\n| 2 [[tablespoons]] parsley\n| 50 ml (2 fl oz) [[dry white wine]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[cornflour]] mixed to a paste with a little cold water\n| Salt and [[freshly ground black pepper]] to taste\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Melt half of the [[butter]] in a pan and gently brown the [[chicken]] pieces on both sides\n| Add the [[lemon juice]], season with [[salt]] and [[pepper]] and return to a gentle heat and cook for 20 minutes\n| Remove the [[chicken]] and keep warm\n| Add the remaining butter, [[onions]], [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[brown]] the [[onions]] being careful not to burn them\n| Add the half of the toasted [[almonds]], [[cornflour]], [[wine]] and return the [[chicken]] and turn the heat up to reduce the liquid so there is just a little sauce\n| Garnish with the remaining almond slices\n| Pour into a warm serving dish\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe hot with [[plain boiled rice]] , garnished with chopped [[parsley]]\n===Variations===\n\nTry 2 tablespoons of chopped [[chervil]] instead of the [[parsley]] if you are growing it or can buy it.\n\nTry with ground [[almonds]] instead of chopped almond flakes\n\n==See also==\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #almondchicken #butter #onions #almonds #cornflour #lemon #parsley #onion #garlic #chervil </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

For recipe that calls for cod, we always use basa\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 820\n|PortionCalories = 205\n|DatePublished=24th June 2014\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  45 minutes\n|PrepTime =  20 minutes\n|CookTime =  25 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Chinese aromatic cod in tomato sauce recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Best with Basa.</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.7</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Make spicy Friday fish-cakes, for a change, make them like this and you'll like them!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Use a Lock and Lock box to coat the fillets.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Use a Lock and Lock box to coat the fillets]]\n\nA highly spiced [[Chinese]]-style recipe that goes brilliantly with [[Mashed potatoes|mashed potatoes]].\n\nAs with any recipe that calls for [[Cod|cod]], we always use [[Basa fillets|basa fillets]] as I think they are tastier and also sustainable.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 4 [[Cod|cod]] fillets, or nicer still, 4 [[Basa fillets|basa fillets]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Sesame oil|sesame oil]]\n}}\n'''dry rub'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 2 tablespoons [[Cornflour|cornflour]]\n| 1 teaspoon freshly [[Ground coriander|ground coriander]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Garlic powder|garlic powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Ginger powder|ginger powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon fine [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Fennel seeds|fennel seeds]], [[Ground|ground]] to a powder\n}}\n'''[[Tomato sauce|tomato sauce]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Garam masala|garam masala]] powder\n| 1 teaspoon [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon freshly [[Grated|grated]] [[Ginger root|ginger root]]\n| 1 teaspoon freshly [[Crushed garlic|crushed garlic]]\n| &#189; teaspoon fine [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Tomato puree|tomato puree]]\n| 175 ml water\n| 1 tablespoon [[Groundnut oil|groundnut oil]]\n| 4 [[Szechuan peppercorns|szechuan peppercorns]]\n| 4 [[Black peppercorns|black peppercorns]]\n| 1 fresh [[Bay leaf|bay leaf]]\n| A very small piece of [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]]\n}}\n'''to serve'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| Freshly chopped [[Mint leaves|mint leaves]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Preheat the [[Grill|grill]] to high\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| MIx the dry rub ingredients together and place in a [[Lock and Lock box]] with the [[Fish|fish]] fillets, close the lid and shake gently to coat the [[Fish|fish]] evenly\n| Once the [[Grill|grill]] is nice and hot, reduce the heat to about half and lightly [[Spray|spray]] a [[Griddle pan|griddle pan]] with [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]] to prevent the fillets from sticking\n| [[Grill]] the fillets for 5 minutes on one side and then spoon the [[Sesame oil|sesame oil]] over the fillets.  Turn and [[Grill|grill]] for 5 minutes on the other side\n| Check the [[Fish|fish]] is properly cooked, set to one side and keep warm\n| Make the [[Sauce|sauce]] by mixing the [[Garam masala|garam masala]], [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]], [[Ginger|ginger]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Salt|salt]], [[Tomato puree|tomato puree]] and water. Ensure the ingredients are well mixed\n| Heat the [[Groundnut oil|groundnut oil]] in a [[Wok|wok]] and add the whole [[Peppercorns|peppercorns]], [[Bay leaf|bay leaf]] and [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]].  [[Stir fry]] for a minute or so\n| Reduce the heat and carefully add the [[Sauce|sauce]] mixture\n| Bring to the [[Boil|boil]], reduce and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 5 minutes\n| Gently add the [[Fish|fish]] pieces to the [[Sauce|sauce]] and [[Poach|poach]] for a few minutes\n| Remove the cinnamon stick and serve\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Mashed potatoes|mashed potatoes]], and garnish with chopped [[Mint leaves|mint leaves]]\n===Variations===\nUse [[Cod|cod]], [[Basa|basa]], or any firm fleshed [[Fish|fish]].  [[Tuna]] would be good too.\n===Chef's notes===\nUse a mild(ish) [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] or reduce the quantities as this might be too hot otherwise.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Freshwater fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#fish #grill #chillipowder #cod #sauce #aromaticcodintomatosauce #cinnamon #mashedpotatoes #groundnutoil #tomatopuree #sesameoil </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

[[Aubergines|aubergines]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 [[Aubergines|aubergines]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Sunflower oil|sunflower oil]]\n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], chopped finely\n| 2 cm [[Root ginger|root ginger]], peeled and [[Julienned|julienned]]\n| 2 tablespoons Thai red curry paste (or to taste)\n|* I recommend [[Cock Brand curry paste]] if you can get it\n| [[Zest]] and [[Juice|juice]] from 1 [[Lime|lime]]\n| 2 tablespoons muscovado [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Light soy sauce|light soy sauce]]\n| 200g [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] (half a standard can)\n| [[Freeze]] the remaining for later use\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Trim the [[Aubergines|aubergines]] and cut into bite-sized cubes\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a pan or [[Wok|wok]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] the [[Onions|onions]], [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Ginger|ginger]] for 3 or 4 minutes\n| Add the [[Aubergine|aubergine]] and [[Saut\u00e9|saut\u00e9]] for 5 minutes or until they start to take some colour\n| Add the [[Curry paste]] and mix well\n| Pour in 400 ml cold water, add the [[Lime juice|lime juice]] and [[Zest|zest]], [[Sugar|sugar]] and [[Soy sauce|soy sauce]] and bring to the [[Boil|boil]].\n| Reduce the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 15 minutes\n| Add the [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] and reheat the [[Curry|curry]], being careful not to [[Boil|boil]] it.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe immediately with [[Plain rice|plain rice]]\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental title": "Baked sea bass (Chinese style)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Baked sea bass (Chinese style) a Chinese recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#fish #blackbeans #springonions #darksoysauce #wine #trout #anchovies #onion #seabass #baking #specialfriedrice \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This is a quick, fresh tasting dish that works brilliantly with sea bass, but most large white-fleshed fish would be just as good\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1118\n|PortionCalories = 279\n|DatePublished=17th January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 1\n |ImageComment = Ready to serve, excuse the test 'hole'!\n |TotalTime = 30 minutes\n |PrepTime = 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 20 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Sea bass in ginger-done.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Love sea bass</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.6</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Expensive, but worth every penny</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:NonLoggedInUser|NonLoggedInUser]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Sea bass in ginger.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Rubbed with sea salt, black pepper and ginger powder]]\nThis is a quick, fresh tasting dish that works brilliantly with [[sea bass]], but most large [[white-fleshed fish]] would be just as good. Carp would be fine if you can get it.\n\nThe time I cooked and photographed this meal I could not get [[spring onions]] or [[black beans]] so I used a small [[onion]], sliced thinly and 4 large [[anchovies]], finely chopped, instead of the [[black beans]].  I also used two small sea bass instead of 1 large.  Moral: Don't go shopping late on a Bank Holiday Sunday! However, it was still a great success.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1  750g (1.5 lbs) whole [[fish]], [[sea bass]], [[trout]] or carp, cleaned and gutted (use two if you can only get small fish)\n| 1 teaspoon [[sea salt]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[ground ginger powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon salted [[black beans]], soaked, drained and crushed lightly, or 4 large [[anchovies]], finely chopped\n| 1 teaspoon [[dark soy sauce]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[sugar]]\n| 1 tablespoon Chinese [[wine]] or [[dry sherry]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[root ginger]], peeled and finely [[shredded]]\n| 2 star anise, broken into small pieces\n| 2 [[spring onions]], [[cut on the diagonal]], or 1 small [[onion]], peeled and finely sliced\n| 2 tablespoons [[vegetable oil]]\n| Sheet of [[tin foil]], large enough to wrap loosely around the [[fish]]\n| '''Dressing'''\n| 1tbs [[light soy sauce]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[sesame oil]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[oven]] to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4), [fan oven 160\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| [[Descale]], rinse and and dry the [[fish]]\n| With a sharp knife make deep cuts across both sides of the [[fish]].  On a very large fish make criss-cross cuts\n| Mix the [[salt]], [[pepper]] and [[ginger powder]] together and rub well into the slashes in the [[fish]]\n| Mix the crushed [[black beans]], [[dark soy sauce]], [[sugar]] and Chinese [[wine]]\n| Sprinkle the shredded ginger and [[spring onions]] on the tin foil and lay the [[fish]] on top\n| Heat 2 tablespoons of [[oil]] until [[smoking]] and carefully pour this all over the [[fish]]\n| When the [[oil]] has cooled a little, spread the [[black bean]] mixture all over the [[fish]] and in the cavity\n| Arrange the broken star anise pieces throughout the cavity of the fish\n| Bring the foil up and seal well and place on a [[baking]] tray\n| [[bake]] for 20 minutes or until the [[fish]] is tender\n| Arrange on a serving platter and pour the [[soy]] dressing over the [[fish]]\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe immediately.\n\nThis is nice with [[special fried rice]] and a [[green salad]]\n===Chef's tip===\nIf you use two small fish instead of 1 large, as long as your tin foil is large enough, it's probably better to use 1 foil parcel for both fish as the flavours seem to mingle better. \n===Variation===\nThis recipe would work equally well with [[trout]].\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#fish #blackbeans #springonions #darksoysauce #wine #trout #anchovies #onion #seabass #baking #specialfriedrice </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Bang, bang chicken, a noisy Chinese recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chicken #bangbangsauce #cucumber #onion #bangbangchicken #garlic #bouquetgarni #unusualrecipes #tea #sauce #chickenstock \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Bang-bang chicken is a deliciously spicy Chinese dish that is easier to make than it first might seem\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 813\n|PortionCalories = 203\n|DatePublished=20th January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = It doesn't look brilliant on the plate, but it was gorgeous & is going on my repertoire!\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 40 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 25 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Bang bang chicken recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Lovely sauce</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Perfect with chicken</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Bang bang sauce.jpg|thumb|300px|right|[[Bang bang sauce]]]]\nBang-bang [[Chicken|chicken]] is a deliciously spicy Chinese dish that is easier to make than it first might seem.\n\nIf you're wondering, bang!, bang! is the noise of the [[wooden mallet]], traditionally used to [[flatten the cooked chicken]] to make it easier to shred.\n\n'''for the chicken'''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 3 skinless, boneless [[Chicken|chicken]] breasts, about 450 g (1 lb) in total weight\n| 1 [[Clove|clove]] of [[Garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| &frac12; teaspoon whole [[Black peppercorns|black peppercorns]]\n| 1 small unpeeled [[Onion|onion]], halved\n| 1 [[bouquet garni]] - optional\n}}\n'''for the garnish'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1 large [[Cucumber|cucumber]], peeled, de-seeded and cut into thin strips. If, like me, you are a lazy cook, slice it in a [[Food processor|food processor]]!\n| 1 serving of [[bang bang sauce]]\n| 1 tablespoon of [[Chili oil recipe (quick)|quick chili oil]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place the [[Chicken|chicken]] in a small saucepan and just cover with water\n| Add the [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Peppercorns|peppercorns]] the [[Onion|onion]] and optionally, the [[bouquet garni]].\n| Bring to the [[Boil|boil]], skim off any scum. Cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 20-25 minutes\n| Remove the [[Chicken|chicken]] and pat dry with a clean [[Tea|tea]]-towel\n| (If making bang bang [[Sauce|sauce]], use 3 tablespoons of the cooking liquid to thin the [[Tahini|tahini]])\n| Freeze the remaining liquid as [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]]\n| Smash the [[Chicken|chicken]] breasts flat with a rolling-pin or the (clean) base of a large [[Frying pan|frying pan]]. Bang! Bang!\n| Shred the [[Chicken|chicken]] with two forks\n| Arrange the [[Chicken|chicken]] and [[Cucumber|cucumber]] on a serving dish and drizzle with [[bang bang sauce]] and [[Chili oil|chili oil]]\n}}\n===Variations===\nI love the combination of spring onions and cucumber, so, although not authentic, I like to add chopped spring onions to this dish, about 6 to go with 1 whole cucumber.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes|Spare ribs]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #bangbangsauce #cucumber #onion #bangbangchicken #garlic #bouquetgarni #unusualrecipes #tea #sauce #chickenstock </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

If you are making in a [[Bread machine|bread machine]], just use the [[French bread]] setting or the longest setting your machine has.\n\n{{RecipeIngredientsTM\n\n}}\n'''For the [[Tang zhong|tang zhong]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 30g [[Strong white bread flour|strong white bread flour]]\n| 150g [[Sparkling mineral water|sparkling mineral water]]\n}}\n'''For the [[Dough|dough]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 7g fast action [[Dried yeast|dried yeast]]\n| 480g [[Strong white bread flour|strong white bread flour]] (I used [[Shipton Mill]] Canadian [[Flour|flour]])\n| 200g water\n| 1 quantity [[Tang zhong|tang zhong]] as above (make up to 170g with water if it has evaporated too much)\n| 1\u00bc teaspoons [[Salt|salt]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Make the [[Tang zhong|tang zhong]] by mixing together the [[Flour|flour]] and water to make a smooth paste. Heat in a saucepan until it reaches exactly 65\u00b0C (149\u00b0F), and remove from the [[Hob|hob]], cover and leave to cool until it is down to room temperature.\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Mix and [[Knead|knead]] the ingredients according to your usual method.\n| Shape into a ball and leave in an oiled bowl, covered, until doubled in size (you can leave in the [[Fridge|fridge]] overnight if you wish, but bring up to room temperature before proceeding to the next stage).\n| Gently deflate the [[Dough|dough]] and repeat the previous step.\n| Deflate once more and shape as desired or place in a [[Banneton|banneton]] or loaf tin.\n| Cover and leave to [[Prove|prove]] until almost doubled.\n| Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 200\u00b0 C (400\u00b0 F - gas 6), [fan [[Oven|oven]] 180\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour].\n| [[Bake]] for 40 minutes adding a tray of [[Boiling|boiling]] water to the bottom of the [[Oven|oven]] to create [[Steam|steam]].\n| If [[Baking|baking]] in a tin, remove the [[Bread|bread]] after 30 minutes and [[Bake|bake]] on a shallow tray, upside down for 10 minutes.\n| Remove from the [[Oven|oven]] and allow to cool on a wire rack before slicing.\n}}\n===Recipe source===\n\n* Idea taken from various recipes by '''[http://lacocinadeloselfos.blogspot.co.uk La Cocina de los Elfos]'''\n===Chef's notes===\nIf mixing in a [[Thermomix]], mix ingredients '''30 seconds / Speed 4''', then '''2 minutes 30 seconds / [[Knead]]'''.  [[Prove]], shape and [[Bake|bake]] as above.\n\nUse menu 21 ''French dough'' (3 hours 35 minutes) on [[Panasonic SD-ZB2502 automatic breadmaker]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Breadmaker recipes]]\n[[Category:Thermomix recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#tangzhong #bake #knead #flour #prove #basicloaftangzhongmethod #dough #sparklingmineralwater #frenchbread #bread #thermomix </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

I'm not so keen on [[bamboo shoots]] so used extra [[carrot]] instead.\n\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 225g (8 oz) [[sirloin steak]] or [[braising steak]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[oyster sauce]] \n| 1 tablespoon [[rice wine]] or [[dry sherry]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[cornflour]]\n| 4100g (4 oz) [[broccoli]]\n| 100g (4 oz) [[bamboo shoots]] - omit and add extra [[carrots]] if preferred\n| 1 [[carrot]], sliced\n| 100g (4 oz) [[button mushrooms]] (or 4 [[dried mushrooms]])\n| 3 slices [[ginger]] root, peeled\n| 1 [[clove garlic, crushed]]\n| 1 dried red [[chili]], crushed\n| 2 [[spring onions]] (scallions) sliced diagonally\n| 4 tablespoons [[vegetable oil]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[light soy sauce]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[sugar]]\n| &#189; pint [[chicken stock]] or water\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| If using [[dried mushrooms]], soak in boiled water for 20 minutes, squeeze dry and discard stalks\n| Cut the beef into very thin straw-like slices\n| Mix the [[oyster sauce]], [[sherry]] and [[cornflour]].  Marinate the beef in this mixture for 20 minutes\n| Cut the [[broccoli]] into small florets and the bamboo and carrots into slices about the same size as the beef\n| Cut the [[ginger]] into match-like sticks\n| Heat the wok and add half of the oil, [[stir-fry]] the beef for 3 minutes. Remove and keep warm\n| Add the remaining oil to the same wok and heat.\n| Add the [[ginger]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[chilli]] and [[spring onions]], followed by the rest of the vegetables, [[sugar]] and [[soy sauce]] and half of the stock\n| Cook for 5  minutes\n| Return the beef to the wok, add the remaining stock and bring to the boil, reduce slightly if to too thin, then serve\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe hot with [[plain rice]] or [[noodles]]\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#beefinoystersauce #ginger #springonions #broccoli #driedmushrooms #carrot #oystersauce #bambooshoots #cornflour #stirfried #chili </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

if necessary to prevent mixture from sticking to pan, add remaining stock\n| Stir [[cornflour]] mixture and add to [[stir-fry]] along with green [[spring onion]] parts and sliced vegetables\n| Bring sauce to a boil\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe immediately with [[Boiled rice|plain boiled rice]].\n===Variations===\nReplace seafood with [[pork fillet]] or [[chicken]]\n{{Template:ThinkPig}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Prawns]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Prawns]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes|Prawns]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes|Prawns]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Prawns]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes|Prawns]]\n[[Category:Shellfish recipes|Prawn]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine|Prawns]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine|Prawns]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#garlic #cornflour #blackbeanprawnstirfry #sesameoil #springonions #chillies #onion #sherry #ghee #seafood #frying </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Bua loy",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Bua loy recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#bualoy #flour #coconutcream #coconutmilk #boiling #boil #dough #coconut #butterfly #thai #pumpkin \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=\u0e1a\u0e31\u0e27\u0e25\u0e2d\u0e22\u0e40\u0e1c\u0e37\u0e2d\u0e01,(Bau Loy). Taro balls in coconut cream is a famous ancient Thai dessert. This is a great recipe for it\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2212\n|PortionCalories = 276\n|DatePublished=31st October 2014\n|Author=Panrapee Satienpisarn\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 8\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  35 minutes\n|PrepTime =  15 minutes\n|CookTime =  20 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Bualoy recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Thank you Panrapee Satienpisarn</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.3</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Very kind of you to add this lovely recipe.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n\u0e1a\u0e31\u0e27\u0e25\u0e2d\u0e22\u0e40\u0e1c\u0e37\u0e2d\u0e01,(Bau Loy). Taro balls in coconut cream is a famous ancient [[Thai]] [[Dessert|dessert]]. \n\nThe main ingredients of Bau Loy are [[Flour|flour]], [[Sugar|sugar]], and [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]]. The definition of [[Bua loy]] comes from the flour, which is moulded in to the pot, put in the [[Boiling|boiling]] water and bring back to the [[Boil|boil]] until it floats Today, Bau loy has a little change from the original by add more ingredients , for example [[Taro|taro]] ,Khai-whan ,or add the colour of flour by using the colour of flowers and food likes, green (Bai-toey), violet ([[Butterfly|butterfly]] [[Pea|pea]]),and black ([[Roasted|roasted]] [[Coconut|coconut]] ),or yellow  ([[Pumpkin|pumpkin]]).\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 cup of thick [[Coconut cream|coconut cream]] obtained by [[Grating|grating]] [[Coconut|coconut]] [[Meat|meat]]\n| 2 cups of thin [[Coconut cream|coconut cream]]\n| 3 cups of [[Sugar|sugar]] (or add more sugar,if you like it very sweet)\n| 4 teaspoons of [[Salt|salt]] [[Flour]] in [[Bua loy|bua loy]]\n| 1 cup of [[Glutinous rice|glutinous rice]] [[Flour|flour]]\n| Colours from food (if you like the colourful)\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Mix the [[Flour|flour]] with water and [[Knead|knead]] it into a [[Dough|dough]]. Make sure it ready to [[Mould|mould]] it into the small balls , check it by touch the dough (the dough will be sticky).\n| Put the balls of [[Dough|dough]] into [[Boiling|boiling]] water and wait until the balls float on the surface of the water, spoon them up and put them in cold water to make them be stable.\n| make creamy [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] by Mixing two cups of thin [[Coconut cream|coconut cream]] with [[Sugar|sugar]] and [[Salt|salt]].\n| place the pot of the mixed [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] on a moderate heat, When it boils, put the balls in it.\n| After that, bring the mixture to the [[Boil|boil]] again, pour the thick [[Coconut cream|coconut cream]] into it and remove it from heat immediately without stirring it.\n| Bau Loy is ready to serve.\n}}\n==See also==\n\n* Pandarin Janesida. How to Cook Bua Loi or Thai Rice Balls in Coconut Milk https://snapguide.com/guides/cook-bua-loi-or-thai-rice-balls-in-coconut-milk/\n* &#3626;&#3641;&#3605;&#3619;&#3586;&#3609;&#3617;&#3627;&#3623;&#3634;&#3609;&#3652;&#3607;&#3618; : &#3610;&#3633;&#3623;&#3621;&#3629;&#3618;(2014) http://www.ezythaicooking.com/free_dessert_recipes/Thai_dumplings_in_coconut_cream_th.html\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Thai recipes]]\n[[Category:Sweets and desserts]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#bualoy #flour #coconutcream #coconutmilk #boiling #boil #dough #coconut #butterfly #thai #pumpkin </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }

with [[Minced|minced]] [[Pork|pork]] ([[Ants climbing a tree]], [[Bean thread noodles with minced pork]] is a classic Szechuan (Sichuan) dish that uses the transparent ([[Mung|mung]]) [[Bean|bean]] thread or cellophane [[Noodles|noodles]] combined with finely minced pork in a spicy [[Sauce|sauce]] that is said to resemble ants climbing a tree.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 125 g (4 oz) [[Dried|dried]] [[Cellophane noodles|cellophane noodles]]\n| 225g (8 oz) finely [[Minced|minced]] [[Pork tenderloin|pork tenderloin]]\n|* Turn [[Pork fillet|pork fillet]] into [[Mince|mince]] in a seconds using a [[Food processor|food processor]] with a metal blade\n}}\n'''for the [[Meat|meat]]'''\n* 1 tablespoon [[Dark soy sauce|dark soy sauce]]\n* 2 teaspoons [[Rice wine|rice wine]] or [[Dry sherry|dry sherry]]\n* 2 teaspoons [[Sesame oil|sesame oil]]\n* 1 tablespoon [[Peanut oil|peanut oil]]\n'''[[Simmering|simmering]] mix'''\n* 1 tablespoon finely [[Grated|grated]] [[Ginger root|ginger root]]\n* 2 tablespoons [[Garlic]], peeled and crushed\n* 4 tablespoons finely [[Chopped spring onions|chopped spring onions]]\n* 2 tablespoons [[Dark soy sauce|dark soy sauce]]\n* 1 tablespoon [[chilli bean sauce]]\n** See chef's note below\n* 2 teaspoons [[Sugar|sugar]]\n* 450 ml (16 fl oz) [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]]\n'''garnish'''\n* Finely [[Chopped spring onions|chopped spring onions]]\n* Finely chopped [[green chillies]] (optional)\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Soak the [[Noodles|noodles]] in warm water for 15 minutes, rinse and drain discarding the water\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Combine the [[Soy|soy]], [[Rice wine|rice wine]] and [[Sesame oil|sesame oil]] with the [[Meat|meat]] and mix well\n| Heat the [[Peanut oil|peanut oil]] until [[Smoking|smoking]] and [[Stir fry|stir fry]] the pork mixture for 2 minutes\n| Add the [[Spring onions|spring onions]], [[Ginger|ginger]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] for a further 2 minutes\n| Add the '[[Simmering|simmering]] mix' and the [[Noodles|noodles]] to the [[Wok|wok]], bring to the [[Boil|boil]] and [[Simmer|simmer]] vigorously until almost most of the liquid has evaporated\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe, garnished with finely [[Chopped spring onions|chopped spring onions]] and optional finely chopped [[green chillies]]\n===Variations===\nYou could make this with fine [[Egg|egg]] vermicelli, if like me, you are not over-keen on [[Cellophane noodles|cellophane noodles]].\n===Chef's note===\nUsing [[chilli bean sauce]] (which in itself is very salty) makes this, extremely delicious dish, a little too salty. I would be inclined to add chilli mash or plenty of fresh chillies instead of the [[chilli bean sauce]].\n{{Template:ThinkPig}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Pasta recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]][[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#cellophanenoodleswithmincedpork #cellophanenoodles #noodles #chillibeansauce #choppedspringonions #garlic #sesameoil #darksoysauce #ricewine #greenchillies #simmering </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

It uses easy to find ingredients and served with rice, is a complete meal.\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 759\n|PortionCalories = 379\n|DatePublished=23rd June 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 2\n|Difficulty = 1\n|ImageComment = Chicken in black bean sauce with brown rice and chives\n|TotalTime = 45 minutes\n|PrepTime = 30 minutes\n|CookTime = 15 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Black-bean-chicken.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Take away taste, at home</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This is better than any takeaway as it does not have that gloopy texture that most takeaway Chinese foods tends to have.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 [[chicken]] breasts\n| 1 tablespoon vegetable oil\n| 2 teaspoons [[sesame oil]]\n| 2 cloves [[Garlic|garlic]], finely chopped\n| 1 tablespoon [[Chinese fermented black beans]]\n| 4 large shredded [[spring onions]] (scallions) chopped diagonally\n| 2 teaspoons [[cornflour]]\n| 1 fresh [[chili]], chopped finely\n| 5 fl oz water or [[chicken stock]]\n| 1 green [[bell pepper]]\n| 2 slices [[ginger]], chopped\n}}\n'''[[Marinade]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1 tablespoon [[rice wine]] or [[dry sherry]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[salt]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Cut the chicken into small cubes, mix with the [[marinade]] and leave for 30 minutes\n| Mix the [[cornflour]] with a little of the water or stock\n| At the same time, soak the salted [[Chinese fermented black beans]] in enough water to cover\n| Chop the [[pepper]] into chunks the same size as the chicken\n| Heat the oil in a wok, add the ginger and [[Garlic|garlic]] stir-fry for a minute\n| Add the onions and chili, [[stir-fry]] for a few minutes\n| Put the chicken and [[marinade]] mix in the wok and fry for about 4 to 5 minutes\n| Add the peppers and fry for a further minute\n| Stir in the beans and their liquid, together with the [[cornflour]], stir often whilst bringing to the boil\n| Reduce to a simmer and cover for 5 minutes\n| Add the [[sesame oil]] and serve\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:IngredientsChicken and green peppers in black bean sauce.jpg|thumb|right|300px|Chicken in black bean sauce, the ingredients\nImage:Black-bean-mix.jpg|thumb|right|Black bean mix\n</gallery>\n\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe hot with [[plain rice]], [[brown rice]] or noodles\n\n==Notes==\nThe version I did for these photos don't quite match the recipe that I normally make but I thought best to leave the recipe as is, and make my excuses here.\n\nWhen shopping, the [[red peppers]] looked better than the green so I switched colours. Lock box]], shake viperously then refrigerate for at least 40 minutes, more won't hurt.\n| Heat a little [[Peanut oil|peanut oil]] in a [[Wok|wok]] and when [[Smoking|smoking]], [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] the [[Chicken|chicken]] slivers for 3 minutes, remove and set aside\n| Add a few tablespoons of [[Peanut oil|peanut oil]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] the [[Garlic|garlic]] until it takes some colour\n| title": "Chicken satay",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Chicken satay recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chicken #chickensatay #chickenthighs #sataysauce #corianderleaves #springonions #ginger #marinade #peanutbutter #cuminseeds #pineapple \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This is my version of Jamie Oliver's Chicken satay his recent book, Jamie Oliver's Comfort Food\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1892\n|PortionCalories = 473\n|DatePublished=4th November 2014\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  12 hours, 40 minutes\n|PrepTime =  12 hours, 20 minutes\n|CookTime =  20 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Chicken satay recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Thanks Jamie!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.8</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Brilliant.  I love this!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n\nThis is my version of Jamie Oliver's [[Chicken]] [[Satay]] from '''Jamie Oliver's Comfort Food''' ''August 2014'', ISBN 978-071815953\n\nI've really just changed some of the ingredients and omitted the unsalted shelled [[Peanuts|peanuts]] as the garnish as Anne does not like peanuts.  She loves [[Satay sauce|satay sauce]] though.  Odd, I know!\n\nAs with any [[Chicken|chicken]] dish, I [[Marinade|marinade]] the chicken pieces in a few tablespoons of [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]], half a teaspoon of fine [[Salt|salt]] and a splash of [[Olive oil|olive oil]].  This was a useful tip picked up on my first [[Indian cookery]] class, many moons ago.  I've also added a dash of [[Dark soy sauce|dark soy sauce]]. My [[Jaccard meat tenderiser]] has been brought into play on chicken for the first time.  We'll see if that makes any noticeable difference.\n\nI've used bone in [[Chicken thighs|chicken thighs]] as they were inexpensive.  These are not idea for skewering so I'll cook them in the [[Oven|oven]] and eat around the [[bones]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 8 [[Chicken thighs|chicken thighs]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]]\n| \u00bd teaspoon fine [[Salt|salt]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Dark soy sauce|dark soy sauce]]\n| 1 teaspoon medium [[Curry powder|curry powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Turmeric powder|turmeric powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon sugar\n| \u00bd teaspoon white [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]]\n| \u00bd teaspoon [[Black cumin seeds|black cumin seeds]]\n| 2 [[Green Indian chillies|green indian chillies]]\n| 2 [[Red chillies|red chillies]]\n| 4 [[Fat|fat]] [[Cloves of Garlic, peeled and crushed|cloves of garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| Thumb-sized piece of [[Ginger|ginger]], peeled and roughly chopped\n| Bunch of [[Spring onions|spring onions]]\n| Bunch of fresh [[Coriander|coriander]]\n| 6 tablespoons crunchy [[Peanut butter|peanut butter]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Tahini|tahini]]\n| 3 [[Limes|limes]]\n| 2 tablespoons of [[Light soy sauce|light soy sauce]]\n| [[Peanut oil]]\n| Small tin of [[Pineapple|pineapple]] rings\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Remove the skin from the [[Chicken thighs|chicken thighs]].  If you're lucky enough to own a [[Jaccard meat tenderiser]], press lots of holes into the [[Chicken|chicken]].  Add the chicken pieces  and [[Marinade|marinade]] for 6 hours of so in a cool place.\n* A few hours before you want to cook the [[Chicken|chicken]], cut some big slashes in them so there are large surface areas for the cover. Pop them in a [[Lock and Lock box]] with the half of the [[Satay sauce|satay sauce]]. Shake well and [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] for a few hours.\n* 30 minutes before you're ready to cook, preheat the [[Oven|oven]] and a [[Griddle pan|griddle pan]] to 200\u00b0 C (400\u00b0 F - gas 6), [fan oven 180\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| De-seed one of each of the [[green chillies]] and one of the [[Red chillies|red chillies]] and peel and roughly chop the [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[ginger]].\n| In a dry pan, heat the [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]] until they pop.  Grind them in a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]] or [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]], pop them back into the pan with the [[Curry powder|curry powder]] and [[Turmeric|turmeric]] for 30 seconds to release the aromas.\n| Reserve a handful of [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]] for garnish and pop the [[Rest|rest]] in a [[Blender|blender]] together with two chopped [[Chillies|chillies]], [[Ginger|ginger]], [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Blend|blend]] to a paste.\n| Add the [[Peanut butter|peanut butter]] and [[Tahini|tahini]], [[Zest|zest]] and [[Juice|juice]] of 2 [[Limes|limes]], 2 tablespoons of [[Soy sauce|soy sauce]], 1 teaspoon of sugar and the green parts of the [[Spring onions|spring onions]].\n| Blend and test for seasoning. Adjust the consistency by adding a little [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]] or water if needed.\n| Reserve half of the [[Satay sauce|satay sauce]] to serve as a garnish, cut a few slashes in the [[Chicken thighs|chicken thighs]], pop them in a [[Lock and Lock box]] with the remaining [[Sauce|sauce]] and [[Marinade|marinade]] in a cool place for a few hours.\n| [[Spray]] the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces with a little [[Oil|oil]], carefully oil the hot [[Griddle pan|griddle pan]] and cook in the [[Oven|oven]] for 20 minutes, turning after 10 minutes.\n| Chop the remaining [[Chillies|chillies]], the white parts of the [[Spring onions|spring onions]] and the [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]] to use as a garnish.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Chicken satay conventional.jpg|300px|thumb|right|Served in a more conventional manner, with a vegetable stir-fry and noodles ([[vegetable chow mein]])\nImage:Chicken satay sspread.jpg|300px|thumb|right|Really should have been with paratha or naan breads but pittas worked pretty well\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with the remaining [[Satay sauce|satay sauce]], [[Lime wedges|lime wedges]], [[pineapple]] rings, [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]] and [[Pitta breads|pitta breads]] or more conventionally with [[vegetable chow-mein]] (stir fried vegetables and noodles).\n===Variations===\nUse boneless [[Chicken thighs|chicken thighs]], chop them into 4 before [[Marinating|marinating]] and cook them on [[Skewers|skewers]]\n===Chef's notes===\nBe aware of food hygiene when preparing this dish as you will be handling raw [[Chicken|chicken]] multiple times and preparing items that will be [[Uncooked|uncooked]] and used as garnishes.\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Mauritian recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental title": "Chicken satay ponorogo",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Chicken satay ponorogo, Barbecue recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#marinade #chicken #sataysauce #spices #peanutoil #brownsugar #grill #jointingachicken #galangal #roasted #jaggery \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=A variant of satay originating in Ponorogo, a town in East Java\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 3050\n|PortionCalories = 381\n|DatePublished=24th October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment =\n|Servings = Serves 8\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  1 hour 25 minutes\n|PrepTime = 1 hour 15 minutes\n|CookTime = 10 minutes \n|Image = [[Image:Peanut sauce.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Different skewers</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">3</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I prefer the street vendor's skewers to these.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nA variant of satay originating in Ponorogo, a town in East Java. It is made from sliced [[Marinated|marinated]] [[Chicken|chicken]] [[Meat|meat]], and served with a [[satay sauce]].\n\nThis variant is unique for the fact that each skewer contains one large piece of [[chicken]], rather than several small slices. The [[Meat|meat]] is marinated in [[Spices|spices]] and sweet [[Soy sauce|soy sauce]], in a process called \"bacem\" and is served with [[Rice|rice]] or lontong (rice cake). The [[Grill|grill]] is made from terracotta earthenware with a hole in one side to allow ventilation for the coals. After three months of use, the earthenware grill disintegrates, and must be replaced.\n\n\n'''[[skewers]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| Wooden skewers soaked in water for 1 hour\n| 450 g (1lb) boneless [[Chicken|chicken]], skin removed and [[Jointing a chicken|cut into pieces]]\n}}\n'''[[Marinade|marinade]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 2 [[Cloves of Garlic, peeled and crushed|cloves of garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| 1 cm (1/2\") [[Galangal|galangal]], [[Grated|grated]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Coriander seeds|coriander seeds]]\n| &#188; teaspoons [[Caraway seeds|caraway seeds]]\n| &#188; teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n| 4 tablespoons [[Peanut oil|peanut oil]] - see variations\n| 2 tablespoons [[Kecap manis recipe|kecap manis]] ([[Indonesian soy sauce]])\n| 1 tablespoon [[Jaggery|jaggery]] or [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]]\n}}\n'''[[Satay sauce|satay sauce]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 4 tablespoons [[Peanut oil|peanut oil]]\n| 225g (8oz) / 1 cup shelled [[Roasted|roasted]] [[Peanuts|peanuts]]\n| 3 hot red [[Chilli peppers|chilli peppers]]\n| 4 [[Roasted|roasted]] [[Pecan nuts|pecan nuts]]\n| 225 ml (1 cup) water\n| 1 teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Jaggery|jaggery]] or [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n\n'''[[Satay sauce|satay sauce]]'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a small pan\n| [[Fry]] the [[Chillies|chillies]] for a minute only\n| Remove from the heat, add the remaining items apart from the water and mix well\n| Allow to cool a little, add to a blender and mix with enough of the water to make a thick paste\n}}\n'''[[Marinade|marinade]]'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Grind the [[Spices|spices]] in a [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]] or a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]]\n| Crush the remaining solid items in a [[Mortar and pestle|mortar and pestle]]\n| Mix with the [[Spices|spices]] and remaining [[Marinade|marinade]] ingredients.\n| Cut the [[Chicken|chicken]] into pieces slightly larger than your thumb - [[Jointing a chicken|see here]].\n| [[Marinade]] the [[Chicken|chicken]] for 1 hour.\n| Traditionally they would be [[Marinade|marinade]]d on the skewers but I find it easier to add the lot to a [[Lock and Lock]]-style box, close and refrigerate, shaking now and then. The [[Chicken|chicken]] can be threaded on to skewers and a final layer of [[Marinade|marinade]] brushed onto the skewers when they are ready to cook.\n| Lay the skewers onto a [[Grill tray|grill tray]] under a preheated [[Grill|grill]] or on a [[Barbecue|barbecue]] and cook for 4 to 5 minutes, turn and re-[[Brush|brush]] with the [[Marinade|marinade]] and cook for a further 4 or 5 minutes\n| Check the juices run clear before serving\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with the [[Satay sauce|satay sauce]], wedges of [[lime]] and [[Rice|rice]] cakes, (plain boilded rice, pressed into 'cakes')\n===Variations===\nIf you can't obtain [[Galangal|galangal]], [[Ginger|ginger]] would probably do at a push.\n\nThe [[Marinade|marinade]] in the authentic version uses [[Rendered|rendered]] [[Chicken|chicken]] [[Fat|fat]] instead of [[Peanut oil|peanut oil]]. \n==See also==\n* http://rumahmakanmurni.blogspot.co.uk/2010/07/sate-ayam-ponorogo-chicken-satay.html\n* http://chickensatay.org/ChickenSatePonorogo.htm\n* http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Satay\n* [[Satay sauce with coconut]]\n* [[Satay sauce]]\n* [[Peanut sauce]]\n* [[Peanut sauce (TM)]]\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Barbecue recipes]]\n[[Category:Indonesian recipes]]\n[[Category:Marinaded]][[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n[[Category:Thai recipes]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#marinade #chicken #sataysauce #spices #peanutoil #brownsugar #grill #jointingachicken #galangal #roasted #jaggery </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Chicken with cucumber",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Chicken with cucumber, Main course recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chicken #cornflour #vegetableoil #cucumber #chickenwithcucumber #wok #garlic #eggwhite #ginger #chiliflakes #specialfriedrice \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=A Chinese-style dish that is quickly stir fried so has a fresh appealing taste\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 733\n|PortionCalories = 366\n|DatePublished=31st October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 2\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 25 minutes\n|PrepTime = 10 minutes\n|CookTime = 15 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Chicken with cucumber recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Tasty!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Unusual and very nice - don't see this in our local Chinese!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\n\nA [[Chinese]]-style dish that is quickly stir-[[Fried|fried]] so has a fresh appealing taste.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| [[Vegetable oil]] for [[Frying|frying]]\n| 225 g ( &#189; lb) skinless [[Chicken|chicken]] breasts\n| 3 tablespoons [[Cornflour|cornflour]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| 1 [[Egg white|egg white]], beaten\n| &#189; medium [[Cucumber|cucumber]]\n| '''For the sauce'''\n| 2 slices of un peeled [[Root ginger|root ginger]]\n| 2 [[Cloves|cloves]] of [[Garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| 2 tablespoons Shaoxing [[Wine|wine]] or [[Dry sherry|dry sherry]]\n| 2 tablespoons water blended with 3 teaspoons [[Cornflour|cornflour]]\n| &#189; teaspoon of [[chili flakes]]\n| &#189; Knorr [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]] cube\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Cut the [[Chicken|chicken]] into cubes (about the size of a [[Sugar|sugar]] cube)\n| Mix with the [[Salt|salt]], coat in [[Cornflour|cornflour]] and mix with [[Egg white|egg white]]\n| Cut the [[Cucumber|cucumber]] is to cubes the same size as the [[Chicken|chicken]]\n| Heat 3 tablespoons of [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]] in a [[Wok|wok]] on a high heat\n| [[Stir-fry]] the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces until cooked (about 3 to 4 minutes), remove and set aside\n| Add a little more [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]] to the [[Wok|wok]]\n| [[Stir-fry]] the [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Ginger|ginger]] until they take a little colour\n| Add the [[Rice wine|rice wine]], [[chili flakes]] and a little more water if more [[Sauce|sauce]] is required, allow it to [[Boil|boil]]\n| Add the [[Chicken|chicken]] and [[Cucumber|cucumber]] back and heat through\n| Add the [[Cornflour|cornflour]] paste and the crumbled [[Stock cube|stock cube]] and stir until thickened\n| Discard the [[Ginger|ginger]] slices and serve\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe with [[Plain rice|plain rice]] or [[Special fried rice|special fried rice]]\n==See also==\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #cornflour #vegetableoil #cucumber #chickenwithcucumber #wok #garlic #eggwhite #ginger #chiliflakes #specialfriedrice </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

They can be cooked from frozen but may take a little longer\n| Spread these evenly on one or two [[Baking|baking]] sheets, sprinkle with a little [[Salt|salt]] and [[Bake|bake]] for 30 minutes until crisp\n| Allow to cool then serve\n}}\n===Variations===\nUse lightly flavoured [[Salt|salt]] for a spicy version \n==See also==\n* [[Preparing a coconut|preparing a fresh coconut]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#coconutchips #coconut #chips #potatopeeler #bake #coconuts #starters #mandoline #juice #baking #miseenplace </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Perfect for Peking duck\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1122\n|PortionCalories = 280\n|DatePublished=3rd August 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4 -  Will make 18 [[pancakes]]\n|Difficulty = 1\n|ImageComment = Commercially made frozen Chinese pancakes\n|TotalTime = 1 hour 3 minutes\n|PrepTime = 1 hour\n|CookTime = 3 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Chinese pancakes.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Does anyone make this?</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">3.7</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Really, you can buy these for a few pennies each - and freeze them, so why bother making them!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nYou can buy [[crispy duck pancakes]] from any [[:Category:Chinese ingredients (supplier)|Asian wholesaler]], usually [[frozen]], or you can make your own using this recipe.\n\nPerfect for [[Peking duck]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 275 g (10 oz) [[plain flour]] plus extra for dusting\n| 250 ml (8fl oz) water, just [[boiled]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[sesame oil]]\n| [[Flour]] for dusting\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a large bowl, add all of the [[flour]] and gradually mix in the hot water, constantly mixing until all of the water has been added.\n| ''Tinker'': If the mixture is too dry, add a little bit more water; too wet, then a tiny bit more flour.\n| Tip the [[dough]] out onto a dusted work surface and hand knead it for almost 10 minutes. As with any [[dough]], tinker some more if needed.\n| Put the [[dough]] back in the bowl to rest for 30 minutes, covered with a damp cloth.\n| Back on to the work surface for another 5 minutes of kneading and tinkering.\n| When you have a smooth, pliable [[dough]], hand-roll into a sausage 45 cm (18\") long and 2.5cm(1\") thick.\n| Chop into 18 equal pieces and mould them into balls. Take two of the balls. Dip one side of one ball into the [[sesame oil]] and put the oiled side on top of the other ball.\n| Mass production! With a [[rolling pin]], roll the 2 pancakes simultaneously into a 15 cm (6\") disc. \n| Put the double pancake into a [[frying]]-pan or [[wok]] on a very gentle heat for a few minutes, really just to dry it out a little.\n| Turn it over and repeat for the other side.\n| Allow to cool, but before it gets cold, peel the two pancakes apart.\n| Do this with the remaining pairs of pancakes.\n| These can be [[frozen]] for later use.\n| [[Steam]] or microwave them to reheat and then serve with [[crispy duck]].\n}}\n==See also==\n* [[Traditional English pancakes]]\n* [[Breton buckwheat pancake recipe]]\n* [[Cr\u00eape recipe]]\n* [[Potato pancakes]]\n* [[Crispy duck pancake recipe]]\n* [[Crispy potato pancakes]]\n* '''Procedure to make a [[How to make crispy aromatic duck at home|complete crispy duck meal at home]].'''\n\n{{CategoryLine}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Steamed]]\n[[Category:Microwaved]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#dough #frozen #sesameoil #flour #steam #pekingduck #crispyduck #pancakes #rollingpin #wok #crispyduckpancakesrecipe </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

A piece of bread should sizzle and brown in a few seconds.\n| Add the greens and fry for 2-3 minutes\n| '''This may need to be done in a few batches''' to prevent the temperature of the oil from dropping too far. Adding too much in one go can cause the oil to froth over the side of the pan which poses '''a severe fire risk'''.\n| Remove from the oil with a [[slotted spoon]] or the mesh basket of the deep fat fryer and drain well on absorbent kitchen paper\n| Place on a heated serving dish, mix the [[salt]] and sugar together and sprinkle evenly over the greens\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\nMake sure the spring greens leaves are well dried by putting in a [[salad spinner]] or wrapping in a clean dry [[tea towel]] and shaking. Any remaining water can detrimentally affect the deep frying process and give rise to an inferior finished product.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Cabbage]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine|Cabbage]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Cabbage]]\n[[Category:Starters|Cabbage]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Cabbage]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Cabbage]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Deep fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#crispyseaweed #deepfrying #frying #teatowel #saladspinner #deepfried #bokchoi #slottedspoon #springgreens </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Dashi stock recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#konbu #katsuobushi #saucepan #dashistockrecipe #litres #dashi #stove #cookipedia #boil #recipesfromothersites #bubble \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This Japanese dashi stock recipe comes to Cookipedia by courtesy of Nik and Edwina's Cookbook\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|DatePublished=29th September 2016\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Katsuobushi [dried shaved tuna] is dashi's key ingredient\n|Servings = 1500ml\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  40 minutes\n|PrepTime =  10 minutes\n|CookTime =  30 minutes\n|TotalCalories = 10\n|PortionCalories = 10\n|Image = [[Image:Katsuobushi_CP.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Hard to find!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">3.6</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Having a job to find katsuobushi. \ud83d\ude1e</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Tantan soup with ramen, pak choi and mad eggs recipe.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Dashi is used in [[Tantan soup with ramen, pak choi and mad eggs]]]]\nThis Japanese [[Stock|stock]] recipe comes to [[Cookipedia]] by courtesy of [[Nik and Edwina's Cookbook]].\n\nOur 2015 trip to Japan, our first ever, was a real eye opener in terms of food. We loved Japanese cuisine, really loved it. Their soups and broths, usually served with noodles (soba, ramen, siratka, udon etc etc) are to die for; a lot of them start with this incredibly simple, incredibly important stock. We buy our konbu (dried kelp seaweed), and katsuobushi (dried bonito flakes) from the Wing Yip supermarket in Shirley, South London. You can also get it online or in person through [[The Japan Centre]]\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 10cm x 10cm piece of [[Konbu|konbu]] \n| 30g [[Katsuobushi|katsuobushi]] \n| 1.5 [[Litres|litres]] of water\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Wipe the [[Konbu|konbu]] with a barely damp cloth if it has a white bloom on it.\n| Put the water in a medium sized [[Saucepan|saucepan]] with the konbu and leave to soak for 30 minutes.\n| Put the [[Saucepan|saucepan]] on the [[Stove|stove]], and start to bring to the [[Boil|boil]].\n| Just as it starts to [[Bubble|bubble]], remove the [[Konbu|konbu]] and discard. Add the [[Katsuobushi|katsuobushi]] and turn the heat to medium.\n| As soon as it starts to bubble, turn the heat off, and leave till all the katsuobushi sinks to the bottom of the pan. Once it has, [[Sieve|sieve]] the liquid, discarding the katsuobushi.\n| It freezes well; we put it in 250 and 500ml containers.\n}}\n===Recipe source===\n\n* https://sites.google.com/site/nikandedwinascookbook/Home/building-blocks/dashi-japanese-broth-stock\n===See also===\n: [[Dashi]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Nik and Edwina's Cookbook recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#konbu #katsuobushi #saucepan #dashistockrecipe #litres #dashi #stove #cookipedia #boil #recipesfromothersites #bubble </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

If you are bothered\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 983\n|PortionCalories = 245\n|DatePublished=23rd October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 25 minutes\n|PrepTime = 10 minutes\n|CookTime = 15 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:My Deep fried chicken in lemon sauce recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Lovely and lemony</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">As good as any takeaway.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Lemon sauce]] is a perfect combination for this dish and although it is Chinese in origin, it works with virtually any other cuisine.\n\nIf you are bothered by [[Deep-frying|deep-frying]], then just pan [[Fry|fry]] the [[Chicken|chicken]] instead.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 350 g (12 oz) skinless [[Chicken|chicken]] breasts\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Shaoxing rice wine]] or [[Dry sherry|dry sherry]]\n| &#189; tablespoon [[Light soy sauce|light soy sauce]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Cornflour|cornflour]]\n| 150 ml (1/4 pint) [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]]\n| 1 [[Egg yolk|egg yolk]]\n| 3 tablespoons [[Plain flour|plain flour]]\n| [[Oil]] for [[Deep frying|deep frying]]\n| '''For the [[Sauce|sauce]]'''\n| 1 to 2 tablespoons of [[honey]] (according to your taste)\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| 3 tablespoons fresh [[lemon juice]]\n| [[Grated]] [[Zest|zest]] and juice from 1 whole [[Lemon|lemon]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Cornflour|cornflour]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Sesame oil|sesame oil]]\n| 150 ml (1/4 pint) [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Slice the [[Chicken|chicken]] into thin slices, width-wise\n| In a small bowl, whisk &#189; a teaspoons of [[Sea Salt|sea salt]], 1 tablespoon of [[Cornflour|cornflour]], 1 tablespoon [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]] and the [[Egg yolk|egg yolk]] so you have a marinade\n| Add the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces, stir and refrigerate for 15 minutes\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] for [[Deep frying|deep frying]] so that a cube of [[Bread|bread]] sizzles within 10 seconds\n| Add the [[Chicken|chicken]] in small batches and [[Fry|fry]] until golden [[Brown|brown]]\n| Remove and drain on kitchen paper\n| In a pan or [[Wok|wok]], mix the [[Sauce|sauce]] ingredients:'' [[honey]], [[Lemon|lemon]] [[Zest|zest]] and juice, &#189; teaspoon [[Sea Salt|sea salt]], [[Sesame oil|sesame oil]], 1 tablespoon [[Cornflour|cornflour]] and the remaining [[Stock|stock]]\n| Heat the [[Sauce|sauce]] gently and stir until it thickens\n| Add the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces back into the [[Sauce|sauce]] and blend well\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Special fried rice]]\n===Chef's notes===\nAfter making this many times, I prefer to serve the sauce as a side-dish rather than mix it up with the fried chicken as the batter tends to go soft.\n==See also==\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine|Chick]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Deep fried]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #sauce #cornflour #deepfriedchickeninlemonsauce #zest #chickenstock #eggyolk #fry #deepfrying #sesameoil #lemon </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Drunken pork",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Drunken pork, Meat recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#pork #drunkenpork #staranise #springonions #garlic #porkvindaloo #beansproutsalad #boiledorsimmered #boil #simmer #ground \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=I did have reservations about this recipe when I first made it as the meat did not appear to be properly cooked\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 726\n|PortionCalories = 181\n|DatePublished=20th January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Nasty, nasty, nasty\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 336 hours, 30 minutes\n |PrepTime = 336 hours\n |CookTime = 30 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Drunken pork.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">DON'T MAKE THIS!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">1</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Horrid and nasty. A waste of good pork.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Drunken pork recipe.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Bring to the boil and simmer for 30 minutes]]\n==Don't bother making this recipe unless you know of a way to improve it!==\nI did have reservations about this recipe when I first made it as the meat did not appear to be properly cooked.  I re-cooked the meat a second time and have now left it for a month or so to 'mature'.  Well the still uncooked meat has seeped out into the wine, giving it a nice bloody-pink colour.  I did try some of the properly cooked meat and it was very tough and had an odd, almost unpleasant flavour.   Not wanting to waste the meat, I tried to use it for a [[Pork vindaloo|vindaloo curry]].  The curry sauce was delicious as always, the pork however was like pieces of wood. Inedible.  I don't have many failures, though this has to be a big one!  I'm sure a better cut of meat such as fillet would improve the texture, but as the flavour was dubious too, I wouldn't bother if I were you.\n\nI have left this recipe as a warning to others - Nasty, nasty, nasty. --[[User:Chef|Chef]] 16:34, 4 August 2009 (BST)\n\nAn unusual way to prepare pork. Slice thinly and serve with rice and a [[beansprout salad]].  It's pickled pork!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1.3 kg boneless rolled  [[Pork|pork]] cut into '''very thin slices''' (see follow-up notes below).\n| Freshly [[Ground|ground]] [[Szechuan peppercorns|szechuan peppercorns]] (use [[Black peppercorns|black peppercorns]] as a poor substitute)\n| 1 tablespoon [[Dark soy sauce|dark soy sauce]]\n| &frac12; tablespoon [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| 2 [[Spring onions, chopped|spring onions, chopped]]\n| 2 [[Fat|fat]] [[Cloves|cloves]] of [[Garlic]], unpeeled and smashed (or to taste)\n| 1 whole [[Star anise|star anise]] [[Clove|clove]] (six petals)\n| 1 bottle of [[Dry white wine|dry white wine]]\n}}\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a pan, just large enough to take the [[Pork|pork]], add the [[Spring onions|spring onions]], [[Salt|salt]], [[Pepper|pepper]], [[soy sauce]], [[garlic]] and [[Star anise|star anise]] and just cover with cold water\n| Bring to the [[Boil|boil]], cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 30 minutes or until properly cooked.\n| Remove the [[Pork|pork]], discard everything else\n| Pat the [[Pork|pork]] dry and leave to drain in a [[Colander|colander]], in the [[Refrigerator|refrigerator]] for 12 hours\n| Cut the [[Pork|pork]] into chunks and place in a [[Sterilised|sterilised]], screw-top-jar.\n| Add the [[Wine|wine]] wine, ensuring the [[Pork|pork]] is completely covered, seal and store in the [[Fridge|fridge]] for 2 weeks\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nDrain the [[Pork|pork]] and serve with a [[Beansprout salad|beansprout salad]] and [[Rice|rice]]\n\nI would suggest keeping the drained wine as a base for other meat-bases sauces.\n===Variations===\nUse a combination of [[onions]] / [[leeks]] / [[spring onions]]\n===Follow-up notes===\n\nMy first attempt was not cooked nearly well enough.  Even after a secondary cooking spell. After a month the blood from the underdone pork started to seep back into the wine.  It would be unsuitable as drunken pork, though it seems to be fine as a base for [[Pork vindaloo]]!\n\nSlice the pork ''very'' thinly next time.  It will also absorb more flavour from the wine.\n\n{{Template:ThinkPig}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Pork]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine|Pork]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Pork]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Pork]]\n[[Category:Pickles and preserves|Pork]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine|Pork]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pork #drunkenpork #staranise #springonions #garlic #porkvindaloo #beansproutsalad #boiledorsimmered #boil #simmer #ground </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
