I have adapted this recipe to my taste\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2754\n|PortionCalories = 688\n|DatePublished=31st October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 12 hours 30 minutes\n |PrepTime = 12 hours 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 20 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Fried Chicken in Sweet Butter Sauce recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Nice sauce</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.7</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Almost sweet and sour. </span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\nAyam Goreng Mentega - ''Fried Chicken in Sweet Butter Sauce''.\n\nI have adapted this recipe to my taste and more easily available European ingredients from a now inactive Wikibooks recipe of the same name.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1.3kg whole [[Chicken|chicken]], cut into small pieces ([[Jointing a chicken|see here]]) - also cut each breasts into 3 pieces\n| [[Oil]] for [[Frying|frying]] ([[Corn|corn]] oil, [[Rapeseed oil|rapeseed oil]], [[Peanut oil|peanut oil]] etc.)\n| [[Juice]] & [[Zest|zest]] from 1 [[Lemon|lemon]]\n| [[Juice]] and [[zest]] from 1 [[Lime|lime]]\n| 2 teaspoons of fine [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n}}\n'''the [[Sauce|sauce]]'''\n* 3 tablespoons of [[Butter|butter]]\n* 2 tablespoons of [[Worcestershire sauce]]\n* 2 tablespoons of light [[Soy sauce|soy sauce]]\n* 2 tablespoons of [[Dry sherry|dry sherry]]\n* 3 tablespoons [[Dark soy sauce|dark soy sauce]]\n* 2 tablespoons of [[Molasses|molasses]] or [[Black treacle|black treacle]]\n* 4 Cloves [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and thinly sliced\n* 4 [[Cloves garlic, peeled and crushed|cloves garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n* 1 small [[Onion|onion]], peeled and thinly sliced\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces to a bowl , add the [[Salt|salt]] and [[Citrus|citrus]] [[Zest|zest]] and juices and [[Marinate|marinate]] in the [[Refrigerator|refrigerator]] for at least a couple of hours. I usually leave them overnight.\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]], pat the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces dry and and [[Fry|fry]] chicken until they are golden, drain on kitchen paper and set to one side.\n| Saut\u00e9 the [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Onion|onion]] for a a few minutes, then add the remaining [[Sauce|sauce]] ingredients.\n| [[Stir fry]] for a minute and then add [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces to reheat.\n| Serve with [[Plain boiled rice|plain boiled rice]], garnished with slices of [[Lime|lime]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Plain boiled rice]], Slices of [[Lime|lime]] and a few chopped [[spring onions]].\n\n===Variations===\nFor a more authentic recipe:\n* Use [[Chinese cooking]] [[Wine|wine]] instead of [[Dry sherry|dry sherry]]\n* Use 8 tbsp Indonesian sweet soy sauce, [[kecap manis]] instead of [[dark soy sauce]] & [[molasses]].\n===Chef's notes===\nFor health reasons, I try to avoid frying whenever I can especially when there is already so much butter as in this recipe.  As a healthy alternative, I sprayed the chicken pieces with a little olive oil and roasted them for about 35 minutes at 220\u00b0C (425\u00b0, Gas 7).  They tasted just as nice!\n==See also==\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}} \n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#friedchickeninsweetbuttersauce #chicken #zest #lime #onion #drysherry #darksoysauce #molasses #juice #garlic #plainboiledrice </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Remove and put to one side.\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a large [[Saucepan|saucepan]] over a medium heat. Stir well.\n| Add the cooked [[Sausages|sausages]] to the pan and [[Simmer|simmer]], covered, for 20 minutes, stirring occasionally.\n| Just before serving, stir in the [[Sugar|sugar]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Plain boiled rice|plain boiled rice]] and maybe a [[poppadum]] or two.\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Thai recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Debbie&andrew's sausage recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n{{Template:DebbieAndAndrew attribution}}\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#currypowder #fruitysausageandcoconutcurry #sultanas #onion #apple #coconutcream #chillipowder #sausages #sunfloweroil #curry #miseenplace </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

It usually served with warm rice\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 975\n|PortionCalories = 243\n|DatePublished=24th October 2014\n|Author=Panrapee Satienpisarn\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  45 minutes\n|PrepTime =  10 minutes\n|CookTime =  35 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Stir fired pumpkin with egg recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Good with courgettes too</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.7</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I made this with courgettes instead of pumpkin and it was rcoking!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Fuk-thong pad khai]] (Fuk-Thong means pumpkin in Thai) or Thai [[Stir-fried|stir fried]] [[Pumpkin]] with [[Egg|egg]] is a delicious and simple Thai dish. It usually served with warm [[Rice|rice]]. Pumpkin is the main [[Ingredient|ingredient]] and when purchasing the pumpkin it must be firm and heavy for its size. The best choice of [[pumpkin]] is Japanese pumpkin (kabocha). It is excellent for using in [[Soups|soups]], [[Stews|stews]] and [[Fry|fry]]. The flavour is sweet and tender. Pumpkin also has [[Vitamin A|vitamin a]], as well as, [[Vitamin C|vitamin c]], [[Phosphorus|phosphorus]], &#946;-carotene, [[Calcium|calcium]] and [[Flour|flour]]. It may reduce the chance of cancer, [[Heart|heart]] disease and anti-ageing.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 150 g [[Minced|minced]] [[Pork|pork]] (or [[Chicken|chicken]])\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Fish sauce|fish sauce]]\n| &#188; teaspoons [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| pinch of [[Pepper|pepper]]\n| 400 g Japanese [[pumpkin]] (kabocha)\n| 2 [[free range eggs]]\n| 1 - 2 [[Cloves garlic, minced|cloves garlic, minced]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]]\n| 1 - 2 tablespoons [[Chopped spring onions|chopped spring onions]]\n| 100 ml water\n| 1 tablespoon [[Oyster sauce|oyster sauce]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| To prepare the [[Pumpkin|pumpkin]], remove [[Seeds|seeds]] and cut off the outside skin of the pumpkin. Then slice the pumpkin into 1-inch cubes and wash well with water.\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a pan and [[Fry|fry]] the [[Garlic|garlic]] until it becomes lightly [[Browned|browned]] and fragrant.\n| Add the [[Minced|minced]] [[Pork|pork]] to the pan wait until the pork nearly cooked.\n| Cut the [[Pumpkin|pumpkin]] and place in a saucepan and cover with water. Bring to the [[Boil|boil]] and cook until tender. When it is soft drain and then add to the [[Pork|pork]].\n| Crack the [[Eggs|eggs]] into the pan.\n| Once the [[Eggs|eggs]] are cooked, stir with [[Pumpkin|pumpkin]] and [[Minced|minced]] [[Pork|pork]].\n| Add the other ingredients: [[Fish sauce|fish sauce]], [[Sugar|sugar]], [[Pepper|pepper]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Onion|onion]], [[Oyster sauce|oyster sauce]] and stir.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServed with warm [[Rice|rice]].\n==See also==\n\n* http://www.allaboutpumpkins.com/perfect.html, How to choose the perfect pumpkin, (4 September 2014)\n* http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2014/09/04/pumpkin-health-benefits_n_1936919.html, huffingtonpost, 8 Impressive Health Benefits of [[Pumpkin]], (7 September 2014)\n* http://shesimmers.com/2013/04/[[Stir-fried|stir fried]]-pumpkin-with-[[Eggs|eggs]]-.html, she simmers, Thai Stir-[[Fried]] [[Pumpkin]] with [[Egg]] (&#3612;&#3633;&#3604;&#3615;&#3633;&#3585;&#3607;&#3629;&#3591;&#3651;&#3626;&#3656;&#3652;&#3586;&#3656;), (7 September 2014)\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]]\n[[Category:Thai recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pumpkin #pork #eggs #fukthongpadkhai #fry #rice #oystersauce #fishsauce #egg #garlic #freerangeeggs </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Way too many onions for a start. Well give it a try, the onions caramelise and just make the dish sweeter.  It's really worth making.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2.5 tablespoons of [[vegetable oil]]\n| 1kg [[belly of pork]] or spare rib chops\n| 1 teaspoon sea [[salt]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[light soy sauce]]\n| 2.5 tablespoons [[hoisin sauce]] \n| 2 teaspoons [[sugar]]\n| 3 [[onions]], peeled and sliced\n| 4 [[spring onions]] (scallions), [[cut on the diagonal]] into 2 \" pieces\n| 4 slices fresh [[root ginger]], finely chopped \n| 290 ml (&#189; pint) stock ([[chicken stock]] is fine)\n| 3 tablespoons [[rice wine]] or [[dry sherry]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Preheat the oven to 200\u00b0C (400\u00b0F - Gas Mk 6 - Moderately hot)\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Cut the belly into 3\" pieces.\n| Sprinkle with [[salt]] and [[pepper]] and rub with 1 tablespoon of [[oil]]\n| Heat the remaining [[oil]] in a wok\n| When hot add the [[ginger]] and the sliced [[onions]] and [[stir fry]] for 4 minutes or until slightly coloured, stirring often.\n| Add all the pork pieces and [[stir fry]] until the surface colour changes, about 4 minutes.\n| Add the [[soy sauce]], [[hoisin sauce]] and the [[sugar]], mix well and mix well.\n| Add the stock and bring to the boil\n| Transfer to a medium sized casserole and place in the oven for 1 hour\n| After 1 hour, reduce the heat to 150 C and leave for a further 1.5 hours\n| Remove from oven, add chopped [[spring onions]] and [[sherry]] and serve\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe with [[Boiled rice|plain boiled rice]]\n===Chef's notes===\n\nI used 1 large [[pork tenderloin fillet]] for 2 greedy people as I prefer it to the more fatty rib cut.  I also added a ladle of the wine vinegar from my my [[Homemade lazy ginger]]\n\n{{Template:ThinkPig}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Pork]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Pork]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine|Pork]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Pork]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#fukienonionsmotheredpork #stirfry #springonions #hoisinsauce #onions #miseenplace #chickenstock #unusualrecipes #vegetableoil #homemadelazyginger #sherry </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Pulse until blended to your liking.\n| Tip out onto a cutting board and make the final mix with your hands.\n| Shape into 8 [[Burgers|burgers]].\n| Place on an oiled [[Barbecue|barbecue]] [[Grill|grill]], hotplate, [[Griddle|griddle]], or even a [[Frying pan|frying pan]].\n| Cook for about 8 minutes, turning every two minutes.\n| Check they are properly cooked.\n| Rest for 4 minutes.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Garlic and ginger pork burgers pulsed.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Pulse a few times - done!\nImage:Garlic and ginger pork burgers in blender.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Add everything to the food processor\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Satay sauce|satay sauce]].\n===Chef's notes===\nUse [[Chili sauce|chili sauce]] if you don't have fresh [[Chillies|chillies]].\n\nFreeze the uncooked burgers, separated with greaseproof paper for easy thawing.\n\nI added a little [[sherry]] and a splash of [[olive oil]] as well, just for the hell of it.\n\nWith in the proportions above, you should not need a beaten egg to hold the burgers together, however, if you increase the quantity of breadcrumbs over 40g , then add a beaten egg at step one.\n{{Template:ThinkPig}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Pork]]\n[[Category:Barbecue recipes|Pork]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine|Pork]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Pork]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Pork]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Pork]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#garlicandgingerporkburgers #sataysauce #barbecue #barbecued #ginger #greensalad #breadcrumbs #burgers #darksoysauce #grill #porktenderloinfillet </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Garlic chicken vermicelli",
                "revisions": [

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Garlic chicken vermicelli Cooking with chillies recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#garlicchickenvermicelli #cornflour #ginger #cabbage #garlic #wok #oystersauce #chickenstock #greenbellpeppers #ricewine #noodles \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This is garlicky variation has been a favourite for many years using items that can probably be found in the freezer, it is quick and tasty and can\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1832\n|PortionCalories = 916\n|DatePublished=31st January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = A version served with Italian spaghetti\n|Servings = Serves 2\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 30 minutes\n|PrepTime = 15 minutes\n|CookTime = 15 minutes \n|Image = [[Image:RecipeGarlic chicken vermicelli.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">You gotta love this!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Creamy and garlicy, yum!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis is garlicky variation has been a favourite for many years using items that can probably be found in the freezer, it is quick and tasty and can easily be modified to use fresh ingredients.\n\nWhy not try [[Jointing a chicken|jointing a chicken]] for this recipe?\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 large skinless chicken breasts\n| 8 oz vermicelli or thin rice [[noodles]]\n| 2\" fresh [[ginger]] root, julienned (cut into matchstick-size pieces)\n| 2 tablespoons [[cornflour]]\n| 4 [[Garlic|garlic]] cloves, minced\n| 1/2 a tablespoon of [[sugar]]\n| 1 cup fresh [[chicken stock]] or Knorr stock cube equiv.\n| 1 tablespoon [[white wine vinegar]]\n| 1 large [[fresh red chili]], chopped\n| &#189; cup frozen mixed vegetables, thawed \n| A quarter of a white [[cabbage]], chopped or slightly more mixed vegetables if cabbage omitted\n| 2 tablespoons [[oyster sauce]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[light soy sauce]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[rice wine]] or [[dry sherry]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[vegetable oil]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Cut the chicken into very thin strips\n| Blend the [[sherry]], 1 tablespoon [[cornflour]] and minced [[Garlic|garlic]] in a bowl\n| Add the chicken strips and leave to stand for 10 minutes\n| Combine the [[vinegar]], [[oyster sauce]], stock, [[sugar]] and remaining [[cornflour]] in a bowl and set aside\n| Cook the vermicelli according to the package directions, omitting any [[salt]]\n| Heat 1 tablespoon oil in a [[wok]] over a medium heat, add the chicken  and fry for 3 minutes; remove and reserve\n| On a high heat, in the same [[wok]], add the remaining  1 tablespoon oil and [[stir-fry]] the chili and the ginger slivers for a few minutes then add the [[cabbage]] and mixed vegetables for a further couple few minutes\n| Add the cooked chicken and stock mixture and cook until it thickens\n| Remove from heat, stir in the [[soy sauce]]\n| Drain vermicelli, arrange on a serving dish and top with the chicken mixture\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe hot\n\n===Variations===\n\nThis variation uses frozen vegetables as they are more likely to be available in a busy kitchen, however, if you have fresh veg, such as red or [[green bell peppers]], [[carrots]], [[courgettes]] etc. then by all means use those. Far nicer than frozen if you have them.\n\nYou can use grated [[ginger]] root or bottled ginger instead of the [[julienned]] ginger.  I just think that with matchsticks of ginger, you get a zesty tang when yo bite into the pieces. \n\n==See also==\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes|Garlic Chicken]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Pasta recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Stir fried]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#garlicchickenvermicelli #cornflour #ginger #cabbage #garlic #wok #oystersauce #chickenstock #greenbellpeppers #ricewine #noodles </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "General Tso's chicken",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=General Tso's chicken Cooking with chillies recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#generaltsoschicken #chicken #wok #springonions #cornflour #sauce #deepfrying #egg #darksoysauce #chilipeppers #kungpochicken \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=General Tso's chicken is a sweet and spicy deep-fried chicken dish that is popularly served in American and Canadian Chinese restaurants where it is\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1201\n|PortionCalories = 300\n|DatePublished=23rd October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 40 minutes\n |PrepTime = 20 minutes\n |CookTime = 20 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:General Tso's chicken recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Complex</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">but was probably worth the effort in the long run.</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The&nbsp;Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n\n'''General Tso's chicken''' is a sweet and spicy [[Deep-fried|deep-fried]] chicken dish that is popularly served in American and Canadian Chinese restaurants where it is erroneously considered Hunan cuisine. The origins of the dish are unclear. The dish was previously largely unknown in China and other lands home to the Chinese. Thus, General Tso's [[Chicken]] is most likely an American invention in the history of American-Chinese food.\n\nThe association with General Tso, or Zuo Zongtang, a Qing dynasty general and statesman, is unclear. The dish is atypical of Hunanese cuisine, which is traditionally very spicy and rarely sweet. Instead, the dish is believed to have been introduced to New York City in the early 1970s as an example of Hunan and Szechuan-style cooking.\n\nThe dish was first mentioned in The New York Times in 1977. It has many similarities to [[Kung Po chicken]].\n\nPeng Chang-kuei, the 98 year old chef who created the much-loved Chinese dish General Tso's Chicken died on 4th December 2016 in Taipei, the capital of Taiwan.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 450 g (1 lb) boneless [[Chicken|chicken]] thighs cut into 2.5 cm (1\") cubes\n| 1 tablespoon [[Light soy sauce|light soy sauce]]\n| 1 beaten [[Egg|egg]]\n| [[Freshly ground black pepper]], to taste\n| 3 tablespoons of [[Cornflour|cornflour]]\n}}\n'''>[[Sauce]]:'''\n* 2 tablespoons [[Dark soy sauce|dark soy sauce]]\n* 1 tablespoon [[Black rice vinegar|black rice vinegar]]\n* 2 teaspoons Chinese [[Rice wine|rice wine]] or [[Dry sherry|dry sherry]]\n* 1 tablespoon [[Sugar|sugar]]\n* 3 tablespoons [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]] or water\n* 1 tablespoon minced [[Garlic|garlic]]\n* 1 tablespoon [[Minced|minced]] [[Ginger|ginger]]\n* 1 teaspoon [[Cornflour|cornflour]] for thickening\n'''>[[Stir-fry]]'''\n* 3 [[Spring onions|spring onions]], [[Chopped on the diagonal|chopped on the diagonal]]\n* 6 [[Dried|dried]] red birds' eye [[Chili peppers|chili peppers]] or to taste\n**[[Peanut]] or [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]] for [[Stir-frying|stir-frying]] and [[Deep frying|deep frying]]\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Mix the [[Egg|egg]], [[Soy sauce|soy sauce]], [[Pepper|pepper]] and [[Cornflour|cornflour]] to make a thin [[Batter|batter]] and coat the [[Chicken|chicken]] cubes. Set aside.\n| Add the [[Sauce|sauce]] ingredients to a bowl and mix well.  Leave for 10 minutes so the [[Sugar|sugar]] dissolves and re-mix.  Set aside.\n| In a [[Wok|wok]], heat the [[Oil|oil]] for [[Deep frying|deep frying]] [180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F)]\n| A few pieces at a time so the [[Oil|oil]] stays hot, [[Fry|fry]] the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces for 3 or 4 minutes until crispy.\n| In a separate [[Wok|wok]], heat 2 tablespoons of [[Oil|oil]], add the chilles and [[Spring onions|spring onions]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] for 40 seconds so the oil is flavoured.  Don't burn or [[Brown|brown]] the [[Onions|onions]].\n| Add all of the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces to the [[Spring onions|spring onions]] and [[Chillies|chillies]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]], shimmying the [[Wok|wok]], for a few minutes to the chicken takes some colour.\n| Stir the [[Sauce|sauce]] well, slide the [[Chicken|chicken]] to one side of the [[Wok|wok]], add the  sauce to the  middle of the wok and mix well to thicken.  Shimmy the wok to coat the chicken pieces with the sauce and serve immediately.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Egg noodles|egg noodles]] and [[Steamed|steamed]] [[Broccoli|broccoli]].  A nice, healthy alternative to egg noodles might be brown rice as I've found it to be a lovely pairing with the other ingredients.\n===Variations===\nSprinkle with [[Dry-fried|dry-fried]] [[Cashew nuts|cashew nuts]].\n===See also ===\n*[http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-us-canada-38181144 General Tso's Chicken creator dies in Taiwan aged 98 ''BBC'']\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Chicken]]\n[[Category:North American recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Deep fried]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#generaltsoschicken #chicken #wok #springonions #cornflour #sauce #deepfrying #egg #darksoysauce #chilipeppers #kungpochicken </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Serve in decent [[Bread rolls|bread rolls]] with a little [[Green salad|green salad]] and [[Satay sauce|satay sauce]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 500g (1/2 lb) of boneless [[Chicken|chicken]] (breast, thighs etc)\n| 2 tablespoons freshly [[Grated|grated]] [[Ginger|ginger]]\n| 2 [[Cloves garlic, peeled and crushed|cloves garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| 4 [[Spring onions|spring onions]], finely chopped\n| 1 fresh red [[Chilli|chilli]], finely chopped\n| 1 tablespoon [[Dark soy sauce|dark soy sauce]]\n| 40 g [[Breadcrumbs|breadcrumbs]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces in a [[Food processor|food processor]] with a metal blade and pulse until you have a rough [[Mince|mince]]. Don't over-do it or you'll end up with baby-food.\n| Add the remaining ingredients and give it a quick pulse.\n| Tip out onto a cutting board and make the final mix with your hands.\n| Shape into 8 [[Burgers|burgers]].\n| Place on an oiled [[Barbecue|barbecue]] [[Grill|grill]], hotplate, [[Griddle|griddle]], or even a [[Frying pan|frying pan]].\n| Cook for about 8 minutes, turning every two minutes.\n| Check they are properly cooked.\n| Rest for 4 minutes.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Satay sauce|satay sauce]].\n===Chef's notes===\nUse [[Chili sauce|chili sauce]] if you don't have fresh [[Chillies|chillies]].\n\nFreeze the uncooked burgers, separated with greaseproof paper for easy thawing.\n\nWith in the proportions above, you should not need a beaten egg to hold the burgers together, however, if you increase the quantity of breadcrumbs over 40g , then add a beaten egg at step one.\n==See also==\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Barbecue recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#gingerchickenburgers #chicken #sataysauce #barbecue #burgers #griddled #ginger #grill #foodprocessor #barbecued #darksoysauce </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Green tea salmon and coconut rice",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Green tea salmon and coconut rice recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#salmon #darksoysauce #marinade #salmonfillets #coconutrice #greentea #preservedlemon #ground #greenteasalmonandcoconutrice #oliveoil #mezzaluna \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This is my take on Jamie Oliver's green tea salmon with coconut rice (from his Jamie's 15 minute meals series).  I'm to accompany this with broccoli\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 3536\n|PortionCalories = 1768\n|DatePublished=30th October 2014\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 2\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  1 hour, 25 minutes\n|PrepTime =  1 hour, 10 minutes\n|CookTime =  15 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Green tea salmon and coconut rice recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">A lot of faff..</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">..but a lot of taste, so it was worth it!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis is my take on Jamie Oliver's [[Green tea]] [[Salmon|salmon]] with [[Coconut rice|coconut rice]] (from his Jamie's 15 minute meals series).  Jamie accompanied his with [[Miso|miso]] [[Greens|greens]], but I'm just going for nice plain [[Broccoli|broccoli]].  I've spiced up the rub for the salmon a little and as I'm not constrained for time I'll [[Marinade|marinade]] mine in [[Dark soy sauce|dark soy sauce]] beforehand.\n\nUsing tea leaves as a herb sound to odd the first time you hear it, but in most cases, herbs are just leaves.  These are sun-dried herby (tea) leaves.be an odd\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 2 small [[Salmon fillets|salmon fillets]] with the skin on\n| 3 tablespoons [[Dark soy sauce|dark soy sauce]]\n| 1 heaped teaspoon of [[Green tea|green tea]] - I used monkey picked oolong\n| 2 teaspoons of [[Coriander seeds|coriander seeds]], freshly [[Ground|ground]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Olive oil]] \n}}\n'''[[Coconut rice|coconut rice]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 150g [[Basmati rice|basmati rice]]\n| 400g tin of [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]]\n| 1 [[Preserved lemon|preserved lemon]] cut in half\n}}\n'''garnish'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1 chopped [[Chilli|chilli]]\n| [[Lime]] quarters\n| Finely chopped [[parsley]] or [[coriander]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Descale the [[Salmon fillets|salmon fillets]] by running a knife at 90 \u00b0 against the '[[Grain|grain]]' of the scales or by using a [[Fish|fish]] descaler\n* Rinse the [[Salmon|salmon]] in cold water to wash off the scales and pat dry\n* [[Marinade]] in [[Dark soy sauce|dark soy sauce]] for 1 hour in a cool place\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Green tea salmon skin removed.jpg|Skin removed ready to fry for a minute to crisp up\nImage:Green tea salmon frying.jpg|Saute the fillets, skin side down\nImage:Green tea salmon ingredients.jpg|The dry rub ingredients\nImage:Descaling a salmon fillet with a knife.jpg|Descaling the salmon fillet with a knife\nImage:Using a Mezzaluna to chop the salmon skin.jpg|Using a [[Mezzaluna]] to chop the salmon skin\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n}}\n'''[[Coconut rice|coconut rice]]'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| ''aim for twice the amount of liquid to [[Rice|rice]] (by volume)''\n| Mix the [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] with 200 ml of water and stir well.\n| Measure 300 ml from this mixture - [[Freeze|freeze]] the remains for next time as you will be making this again!\n| Rinse the [[Basmati rice|basmati rice]] for a few minutes under cold running water\n| Add 300 ml of the coconut mixture, the [[Rice|rice]] and the [[Preserved lemon|preserved lemon]] to the pan, bring to the [[Boil|boil]], reduce to a [[Simmer|simmer]], cover and cook for 10 minutes without stirring\n| After 10 minutes, remove from the heat and discard the [[Preserved lemon|preserved lemon]]\n}}\n'''[[Green tea|green tea]] [[Salmon|salmon]]'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat a [[Frying pan|frying pan]] with 1 teaspoon of [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| My green [[Tea leaves|tea leaves]] were monkey picked oolong which are quite large so I added them to the whole [[Coriander seeds|coriander seeds]], [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] and [[Ground|ground]] them to a powder in my [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]]\n| Sprinkle the [[Ground|ground]] powder onto a plate\n| Remove the [[Salmon|salmon]] from the [[Soy|soy]] [[Marinade|marinade]] and discard the marinade\n| Dredge the [[Salmon|salmon]] through the rub and ensure it is evenly coated, skin included\n| Lay the [[Salmon fillets|salmon fillets]], skin side down and [[Saute|saute]] for 5 minutes, jiggle the [[Salmon|salmon]] after a few minutes to ensure it does not stick, but don't be tempted to turn it over yet\n| After 5 minutes, [[Saute|saute]] the [[Salmon|salmon]] on the other three sides for about a minute each side\n| Carefully remove the [[Salmon fillets|salmon fillets]] from the pan and place skin side up on a chopping board\n| Using a sharp knife, peel the skin from the fillets\n| Place the skin back into the pan, soft side down for 1 minute so it can crisp up. Press it into the pas so it makes good contact with the heat.\n| Pat the skin with a paper towel to remove any excess oil\n| Cut the skin into 2.5 cm slices to arrange over the dish like crisps when served.  A [[Mezzaluna]] is a great tool to use for this.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Broccoli|broccoli]]\n===Recipe source===\n* My variation on [http://hotcooking.co.uk/recipes/70/jamie-oliver-15-minute-meals-green-tea-salmon Jamie Oliver's Green tea salmon]\n===Variations===\nMy favourite [[marinade]] for this dish is now 3 tablespoons of [[dark soy sauce]], 1 tablespoon of [[Chinkiang rice vinegar]] (''Black rice vinegar'') and a small splash of [[olive oil]].\nYou can use a fresh [[Lemon|lemon]] for the rice if you don't have [[Preserved lemons|preserved lemons]]\n===Chef's notes===\nThis was so good that we had this three times in one week!\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Freshwater fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#salmon #darksoysauce #marinade #salmonfillets #coconutrice #greentea #preservedlemon #ground #greenteasalmonandcoconutrice #oliveoil #mezzaluna </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

teaspoon [[salt]]\n| 2 free-range [[eggs]]\n}}\n'''for thickening'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 3 tablespoons [[white wine vinegar]]\n| 1.5 tablespoons [[dark soy sauce]]\n| &#189; teaspoon freshly ground [[black pepper]]\n| 3 tablespoons [[cornflour]] blended to a paste with 3 tablespoons of water\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Soak the mushrooms in boiled water for 20 minutes, squeeze excess water, remove stalks and slice thinly\n| Shred the cooked meat and [[bamboo shoots]]\n| Beat the [[eggs]]\n| Mix together the thickening ingredients\n| Heat the stock in a large pan\n| Add everything but the [[eggs]] and thickening, bring to the boil, cover simmer for 5 minutes\n| Pour in the thickening and stir until the consistency changes\n| Stir the soup so it rotates and gradually pour the [[eggs]] into the soup in a thin stream\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe immediately\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Egg recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#hotandsoursoup #eggs #bambooshoots #whitewinevinegar #chicken #cornflour #ham #boiledorsimmered #darksoysauce #chinesemushrooms #blackpepper </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

You can eat a whole duck for next to nothing this way. :D</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Chopped cucumber - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|[[Cucumber]], chopped|300px|thumb|right|Chopped [[cucumber]]]]\n[[Image:Chopped spring onions - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|Spring onions, chopped|300px|thumb|right|[[Chopped spring onions]]]]\n[[Image:Chinese pancakes.jpg|300px|thumb|right|Frozen Chinese pancakes]]\n[[Image:Ready to go! - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|300px|thumb|right|Ready to go!]]\n''Please note:  This recipe shows how to cook a '''ready prepared Peking-style duck''' and serve with the standard accompaniments.   [[Peking duck|See here]] if you want to create this recipe from scratch using a fresh [[duck]].'' \n===A step by step guide, in pictures===\n<gallery widths=270px heights=270px perrow=5>\nImage:Spring onions - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|2 massive [[spring onions]]\nImage:Chopping spring onions - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|[[Cheat]], chop the [[spring onions]] in a [[food processor]]\nImage:Chopped spring onions - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|Spring onions, chopped\nImage:Pretty-up the cucumber - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|Pretty-up the [[cucumber]]\nImage:De-seed the cucumber- making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|De-seed the [[cucumber]], if you wish\nImage:Chopping the cucumber - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|[[Cheat]], chop the [[cucumber]] in a [[food processor]]\nImage:Chopped cucumber - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|[[Cucumber]], chopped\nImage:Crispy duck - cook from frozen - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|Aromatic duck, cook from frozen\nImage:Duck ready for the oven - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|Aromatic duck, ready for the over (200\u00b0 C for 45 minutes)\nImage:Crispy duck cooked - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|Aromatic duck. Cooked\nImage:Shred the duck - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|Shred the duck with two forks\nImage:Crispy duck pancakes- making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|[[Crispy duck pancakes]]\nImage:Warm the pancakes in the microwave- making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|Warm them for a few seconds in the [[microwave]]\nImage:Sauce selection - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|The sauce selection\nImage:Ready to go! - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|Ready to go\nImage:Spread the sauce - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|Spread the sauce\nImage:Sprinkle the spring onions - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|Sprinkle the [[spring onions]] on the pancake\nImage:Add the cucumber - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|Add the sliced [[cucumber]]\nImage:Add the shredded crispy duck - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|Top with shredded aromatic crispy duck\nImage:Ready to eat! - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|Rolled up and ready to eat\n</gallery>\n\nMaking this delicious Chinese take-away favourite at home is so simple and so reasonably priced that you'll never buy it from the take-away again.\n\nUnless you want to spend money for the sake of it, don't buy the ingredients from your local 'big-name' supermarket.  You'll probably pay double and certainly won't have the selection of ingredients that you'll have if you follow my next suggestion.\n===Buy the ingredients from the same place as your Chinese take-away does===\n''This advice is specific to the United Kingdom, though I'm sure similar outlets exist throughout the world''.\n\nPay a visit to your local [[Chinese food wholesaler]].  There are chains of them throughout the UK and you don't need to be a member of any trade association to buy from them.  You may find them a little intimidating at first, but the staff are friendly and if you are into your food in a big way, you will find it a fascinating experience.  Most of them have a very good online presence so you can 'look before you buy'.  I guarantee that you will go back again and again.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 800g frozen pre cooked aromatic crispy duck [\u00a39.50]\n| 1 multi-pack 'pancakes for crispy duck' [ 102 pancakes, 17 packs (pre-packed in packs of 6) ]\n| 1 [[cucumber]]\n| 1 bunch [[spring onions]]\n| 50g 'Sauce for Peking Duck'\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Defrost a few packets of [[Chinese pancakes]]\n* Peel the [[cucumber]], quarter lengthwise and run a sharp knife along each quadrant to remove most of the seeds.\n* Top and tail the [[spring onions]]\n* Using a [[food processor]] with a metal blade, slice the [[cucumber]] and [[spring onions]].  It doesn't look as neat as [[julienning]] them, but it takes a quarter of the time and tastes just as good.\n* Chill the [[spring onions]] and [[cucumber]] in the [[refrigerator]] while the [[duck]] defrosts\n* Preheat the oven to 200\u00b0 C (400\u00b0 F - gas 6)\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place the [[duck]] (skin-side down) on a rack over a [[roasting tray]] or a [[perforated roasting tray]] over a [[roasting tray]] - this will allow for the fat to drain off whilst the [[duck]] cooks.\n| Roast the [[duck]] for 45 minutes, turning once, carefully draining the roasting tray if it fills with [[fat]], otherwise you'll have a very smoky kitchen\n| You can [[steam]] the pancakes in a [[Chinese steamer]] over a [[wok]] or pan of boiling water for a few minutes - they only need to be warmed, not cooked.  I find they often stick together warming them this way so I prefer to separate the pancakes, spread them out on a large plate and [[microwave]] them for a minute or two to warm them.\n| Remove the [[duck]] from the oven, chop the skin into bite-sized pieces and then with two forks pulling against each other, shred the duck meat.\n}}\n===To serve===\nSpread a little of your favourite sauce on a pancake, cover with cucumber, spring onions & duck, roll the pancake up and eat with your fingers - delicious!\n===Variations===\nTry other sauces: [[Hoisin sauce]], [[Plum sauce]], [[chilli sauce]] and even [[mayonaise]] works very well!\n\nSliced white [[onions]] are a nice addition to [[spring onions]].\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Duck]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes|Duck]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes|Duck]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes|Duck]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine|Duck]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Duck]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Duck]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Steamed]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#cucumber #springonions #duck #howtomakecrispyaromaticduckathome #foodprocessor #roastingtray #microwave #cheat #chinesepancakes #miseenplace #unusualrecipes </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

I think the best restaurant meal I ever had was an Indonesian banquet one new-years' eve, in Docklands, in the Yuppie 80's - avec Filofax!  This recipe was probably included in one of the seemingly 100's of dishes.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 675 g (1.5 lb) [[sirloin steak]], trimmed of [[Fat|fat]]\n| 3 tablespoons [[Groundnut oil|groundnut oil]]\n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], peeled and sliced\n| 3 [[Fat|fat]] [[Garlic cloves, peeled and crushed|garlic cloves, peeled and crushed]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Ground|ground]] [[Ginger|ginger]]\n| 1 teaspoon white [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]], freshly [[Ground|ground]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Coriander seeds|coriander seeds]], freshly [[Ground|ground]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]]\n| 150 ml [[Shredded|shredded]] [[Coconut|coconut]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Jaggery|jaggery]] or [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]]\n| 284 ml (&frac12; pint) [[Beef Stock|beef stock]]\n}}\n''' garnish'''\n* Thin slivers red [[Sweet pepper|sweet pepper]]\n* Chopped [[Green chillies|green chillies]]\n* [[Spring onions]]\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat 3/4 of the [[Oil|oil]] in a [[Wok|wok]] and add the sliced [[Onions|onions]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] and gently saut\u00e9 for 6 minutes.\n| Reserve the onions and garlic to a separate plate, add the remaining oil, turn the heat up a little and [[Brown|brown]] the [[Beef|beef]].\n| Add the [[Spices|spices]] and stir [[Fry|fry]] for a minute.\n| Add everything back to the wok, add the [[Sugar|sugar]], [[Coconut|coconut]], [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]] and [[Beef Stock|beef stock]], bring to the [[Boil|boil]] then immediately reduce the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] uncovered for 35 minutes. Stir now and then and keep a watchful eye to ensure it does not stick and burn.  By this time most of the liquid should have reduced.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Plain boiled rice|plain boiled rice]], garnished with [[Red peppers|red peppers]], [[Onions|onions]] and [[Chillies|chillies]]. \n===Chef's notes===\nUse pre-[[Ground|ground]] [[Spices|spices]] if you don't have the whole [[Spices|spices]].\n===Coconut shredder working in a 10 second video=== \n<YouTube>https://www.youtube.com/embed/-0Ha0o0Xy5Q</YouTube>\n===Chef's notes===\nI've used a mixture of [[Dried|dried]] coconut flakes and desiccated coconut plus a few tablespoons of [[coconut block]] to make it extra coconutty, without adding extra liquid.\n\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Indonesian recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#ground #indonesiancoconutbeef #spices #fat #lemonjuice #coconut #onions #beefstock #dried #cuminseeds #corianderseeds </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Khanom Tom",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Thai coconut balls (Khanom Tom), Thai dessert recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#khanomtom #coconut #grated #pandanus #flour #dough #glutinousrice #brownsugar #juice #dessert #coconutcream \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Khanom Tom (Thai : \u0e02\u0e19\u0e21\u0e15\u0e49\u0e21) or coconut balls are a very old Thai dessert from the Sukhothai period and are used for auspicious ceremonies\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1739\n|PortionCalories = 217\n|DatePublished=30th October 2014\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 8\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  30 minutes\n|PrepTime =  20 minutes\n|CookTime =  10 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:glutinous rice balls for dessert.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n}}\n[[Khanom Tom]] ([[Thai]] : \u0e02\u0e19\u0e21\u0e15\u0e49\u0e21) or [[Coconut|coconut]] balls are a very old Thai [[Dessert|dessert]] from the Sukhothai period and are traditionally used for auspicious ceremonies. Khanom tom consist of [[Glutinous rice|glutinous rice]] [[Flour|flour]] , [[Grated|grated]] coconut , [[Pandanus|pandanus]] [[Juice|juice]] , [[Salt|salt]] , and [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]]. Khanom Tom is sweet-smelling, sweet and the texture is smooth ,soft and sticky.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 cup [[Glutinous rice|glutinous rice]] [[Flour|flour]] \n| 2 tablespoons [[Coconut cream|coconut cream]] \n| 100 grams white [[Grated|grated]] [[Coconut|coconut]] (for the filling) \n| 1 cup white [[Grated|grated]] [[Coconut|coconut]] (for the coating) \n| \u00bd cup [[Sugar|sugar]] \n| \u00bd teaspoon [[Salt|salt]] \n| \u00bc cup thick [[Pandanus|pandanus]] [[Juice|juice]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Putting the [[Grated|grated]] [[Coconut|coconut]] in the pot and [[Steam|steam]] until hot.\n| Mix in the [[Salt|salt]] and set aside.\n| Make a filling by mixing [[Grated|grated]] [[Coconut|coconut]] with [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]] on a medium heat and stir until the [[Sugar|sugar]] has dissolved\n| Remove from the heat, allow to cool a little and make by [[Hand|hand]] into small balls.\n| Make the [[Dough|dough]] by [[Kneading|kneading]] [[Glutinous rice|glutinous rice]] [[Flour|flour]] , [[Coconut cream|coconut cream]] , [[Pandanus|pandanus]] juice and a little water.\n| Make the [[Dough|dough]] into a ball and press to flatten. Fill with the filling and wrap dough to cover it.\n| [[Boil]] the [[Dough|dough]] to ball in. You can [[Scoop|scoop]] out them when they float. Lastly, roll with the [[Steamed|steamed]] [[Grated|grated]] [[Coconut|coconut]].\n}}\n===Recipe source===\n\n* [[Khanom Tom]] - [[Pandanus]] [[Rice]] Balls,(n.d.), Retrieved October 15,2014 [https://www.achefshelp.com/recipe/331/pandanus-rice-ballskhanom-tom-bai-toei-[[Dessert|dessert]]-[[Thailand|thailand]]-worldwide-recipes]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">No accounting for taste</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">2</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Not for me I'm afraid.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Thai recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Sweets and desserts]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Steamed]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#khanomtom #coconut #grated #pandanus #flour #dough #glutinousrice #brownsugar #juice #dessert #coconutcream </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Kongnamul kuk bap",
                "revisions": [

                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Kongnamul kuk bap, Vegetarian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#kongnamulkukbap #rice #egg #beansprouts #springonion #chillipowder #garlic #sesameoil #unusualrecipes #blanching #toastedsesameseeds \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=A spicy breakfast dish of rice from the city of Chonju in the south-west of Korea\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 487\n|PortionCalories = 243\n|DatePublished=24th October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 2\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 20 minutes\n |PrepTime = 10 minutes (incl cooling)\n |CookTime = 10 minutes (cooking rice)\n |Image = [[Image:Kongnamul kuk bap recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Most definitely Oriental</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.6</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">And unusual, but rather good too.</span> \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nA spicy breakfast dish of [[Rice|rice]] from the city of Chonju in the south-west of Korea.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 tablespoon [[Sesame oil|sesame oil]]\n| [[Garlic]] to taste, finely [[Diced|diced]]\n| 1 [[Spring onion|spring onion]], sliced\n| 182 ml [[Rice|rice]], cooked\n| 25 g [[Bean sprouts|bean sprouts]], [[Blanched|blanched]] in [[Boiling|boiling]] water for 2 minutes\n| 240 ml water from [[Blanching|blanching]] the [[Bean sprouts|bean sprouts]] \n| &frac14; teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n| 1 large [[Egg|egg]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Toasted sesame seeds|toasted sesame seeds]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]], or to taste\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a saucepan, heat the [[Sesame oil|sesame oil]] and gently [[Fry|fry]] the [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Spring onion|spring onion]] until soft.\n| Add the [[Rice|rice]], [[Bean sprouts|bean sprouts]], hot water and [[Salt|salt]] and mix well.\n| Then add the [[Sesame seeds|sesame seeds]] and [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] and break the [[Egg|egg]] over the mixture.\n| Bring to the [[Boil|boil]] over a medium heat and cook for 2 minutes, without stirring.\n| Finally, stir the [[Egg|egg]] into the mixture and remove from the heat.\n| Serve hot.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nThis can be accompanied by a [[Cabbage|cabbage]] or [[Radish|radish]] [[Kimchi|kimchi]].  Although this is actually a breakfast dish, you may wish to serve it as an [[Accompaniment|accompaniment]] to a [[Main course|main course]].\n===Chef's notes===\nThe Koreans generally use a medium-grained [[Rice|rice]], as they are not so fond of [[Basmati]] or long-grained rice as the latter varieties are of course found mainly in India and the Middle East.  However, I did in fact use Basmati.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Kongnamul kuk bap]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Kongnamul kuk bap]]\n[[Category:Korean recipes|Kongnamul kuk bap]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine|Kongnamul kuk bap]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes|Kongnamul kuk bap]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Kongnamul kuk bap]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Kongnamul kuk bap]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Kongnamul kuk bap]]\n[[Category:Breakfast recipes|Kongnamul kuk bap]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#kongnamulkukbap #rice #egg #beansprouts #springonion #chillipowder #garlic #sesameoil #unusualrecipes #blanching #toastedsesameseeds </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Kuay Teow Kua Gai",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Kuay Teow Kua Gai (Fried rice noodles with chicken) recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#kuayteowkuagai #chicken #oystersauce #lettuce #squid #vinegar #tomato #ricenoodles #cabbage #lightsoysauce #wok \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Fried rice noodles with chicken or Kuay Teow Kua Gai (Thai : \u0e01\u0e4b\u0e27\u0e22\u0e40\u0e15\u0e35\u0e4b\u0e22\u0e27\u0e04\u0e31\u0e48\u0e27\u0e44\u0e01\u0e48) is a Chinese-influenced dish with Noodles\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1928\n|PortionCalories = 482\n|DatePublished=23rd October 2014\n|Author=Panrapee Satienpisarn\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  10 minutes\n|PrepTime =   5 minutes\n|CookTime =  5 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Kuay Teow Kua Gai recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n}}\nStir-fried [[rice noodles]] with [[chicken]], Fried rice noodles with [[chicken]] or Kuay Teow Kua Gai (Thai : \u0e01\u0e4b\u0e27\u0e22\u0e40\u0e15\u0e35\u0e4b\u0e22\u0e27\u0e04\u0e31\u0e48\u0e27\u0e44\u0e01\u0e48) is a Chinese-influenced dish with Noodles or Kuay Teow that is popular in Thailand. Kuay teow was later modified by Thais to dried noodles with chicken. Then, they call this style \"Kuay Teow Kua Gai\". Kuay Teow Kua Gai normally is served as soaked dried rice noodles stirred with a simple combination of ingredients, such as [[chicken]], [[squid]] and [[lettuce]]. You can add other additional ingredients as sliced [[tomatoes]], [[egg]], deep-fried doughstick, [[garlic]]  and [[spring onion]]. It is seasoned with [[oyster sauce]], [[light soy sauce]] and fish sauce. It also may be seasoned with sauce prik (''nam prik - [[chilli sauce]]''), [[chili flakes]], [[vinegar]], [[sugar]] and tangy [[tomato sauce]].\n\nTo make this dish special is arrange the Kuay Teow Kua Gai on the top of [[lettuce]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n|\u00bd kilo of [[rice noodle]] (Depends on you)\n|\u00bd cup of sliced chicken\n|\u00bd cup of [[squid]] \n|3 chicken [[eggs]] \n|Sliced [[Tomato]]\n|1 teaspoon of dry [[cabbage]] leaves\n|1 tablespoon of chopped [[spring onions]]\n|2-3 tablespoons of frying [[oil]]\n|1 tablespoon of [[oyster sauce]]\n|1 tablespoon of [[fish sauce]]\n|2 tablespoons of [[oyster sauce]]\n|1 tablespoon of [[soy sauce]]\n|1 tablespoon of [[white sugar]]\n|[[Chinese cabbage]] (depends on you)\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the oil to your [[wok]]\n| Add the onions and vegetables and stir fry for 3 minutes\n| Add the meat or fish and stir fry for a few more minutes\n| Pour in the liquid ingredients and mix well\n| ''You can add the egg and scramble it in the pan, then mix it up, or just add it and stir-fry it as it cooks''\n}}\n\n\n=== See also ===\n\n*http://www.ucancookthai.com/language-thai/th-recipes/th-noodle/content-th-stir fried-chicken-noodle.htm  ,\u0e01\u0e4b\u0e27\u0e22\u0e40\u0e15\u0e35\u0e4b\u0e22\u0e27\u0e04\u0e31\u0e48\u0e27\u0e44\u0e01\u0e48 (October 06, 2009) <br>\n*http://naeskitchen.blogspot.com/2010/03/fried-rice-noodles-with-chicken-thai.html ,\u0e01\u0e4b\u0e27\u0e22\u0e40\u0e15\u0e35\u0e4b\u0e22\u0e27\u0e04\u0e31\u0e48\u0e27\u0e44\u0e01\u0e48 - Fried rice noodles with chicken Thai style - Massa de arroz frita com galinha (Nae's Kitchen, MARCH 29, 2010)\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Looks and tastes authentic</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.7</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Putting this on a bed of lettuce sounded odd, but it works really well, strangely.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Egg recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]]\n[[Category:Thai recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#kuayteowkuagai #chicken #oystersauce #lettuce #squid #vinegar #tomato #ricenoodles #cabbage #lightsoysauce #wok </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Kuay Teow Lot in the mean in Thai is a [[Noodle|noodle]] tube shape, but actuality it doesn't look like a tube. Why then did they choose this name? May be in the past they like to use a sheet of [[Noodles|noodles]] and add the filling then roll it. The shape will be thin and long look like a tube, but nowadays people like to wrap it in a square size fit mouth same as Miang Kham, Kuay Teow Lui Suan or Fresh spring roll.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| Sheet of [[Noodle|noodle]] \u00bd kg \n| [[Minced]] [[Pork|pork]] 700 g \n| [[Shrimp]] 500 g \n| [[Mushroom]] 200 g\n| [[Tofu]] 2 sheets\n| [[Pickle]] [[Turnip|turnip]] \u00bc cup\n| Water 3 cup\n| [[Garlic]] 2 tablespoon\n| [[Coriander]] root 1 tablespoon\n| [[Oil]] 2 tablespoon\n| [[Light soy sauce]] \u00bc cup\n| [[Dark soy sauce]] 1 tablespoon\n| [[Oyster sauce]] 2 tablespoon\n| [[Sugar]] \u00bd cup\n| [[Carrot]] 150 g\n| [[Bean sprouts]] 1 kg\n| [[Lettuce]] 200 g\n}}\n'''sauce'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| [[Chilli]] 1 g\n| [[Garlic]] 1 tablespoon\n| [[Vinegar]] 1/3 cup\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Heat [[Oil|oil]] in the pan and [[Fry|fry]] [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Onion|onion]], [[Coriander|coriander]] [[Roots|roots]], [[Tofu|tofu]], [[Minced|minced]] [[Pork|pork]], [[Shrimp|shrimp]], [[Mushroom|mushroom]] and [[Lettuce|lettuce]] fry together \n| [[Boiling]] three cups of water, add a [[Carrot|carrot]] cut into a small square pieces and then [[Boil|boil]] until soft. Put an ingredient from the first stage into the pot and mix together and then season with a [[Light soy sauce|light soy sauce]], [[Dark soy sauce|dark soy sauce]], [[Oyster sauce|oyster sauce]] and [[Sugar|sugar]] when it boils take off the [[Stove|stove]]. \n| Put the mixture onto a [[Noodle|noodle]] sheets then roll it to be tight. Next [[Steam|steam]] for about 3 minutes when finish slice as you like decorating your plate with [[Lettuce|lettuce]].\n| Finally eat with [[Sauce|sauce]].\n}}\n===Recipe source===\n\n* \u0e23\u0e34\u0e0d \u0e40\u0e08\u0e23\u0e34\u0e0d\u0e28\u0e34\u0e23\u0e34, \u0e2d\u0e17\u0e34\u0e15\u0e14\u0e32 \u0e1a\u0e38\u0e0d\u0e1b\u0e23\u0e30\u0e40\u0e14\u0e34\u0e21 (September 1,2008) \u201c[[Kuay Teow Lot]]\u201d http://www.doctor.or.th/article/detail/5756\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Steamed]]\n[[Category:Thai recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#kuayteowlot #garlic #noodle #lettuce #shrimp #pork #carrot #tofu #oystersauce #darksoysauce #coriander </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Kung Po chicken",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Kung Po chicken, Chinese recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#kungpochicken #chicken #carrots #cornflour #toasted #eggfriedrice #onions #garlic #sesameoil #cashewnuts #wok \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Kung Po chicken (also spelled Kung Pao chicken) is a classic dish in Szechuan cuisine, originating in the Sichuan Province of central western China\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1185\n|PortionCalories = 296\n|DatePublished=31st January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |ImageComment = Kung po chicken & [[egg fried rice]]\n |TotalTime = 1 hour\n |PrepTime = 40 minutes\n |CookTime = 20 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Kung po chicken recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">My favourite Chinese meal</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Nicer than the gloopy versions sold at some take-aways.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]])</span></span>\n }}\nKung Po chicken (also spelled Kung Pao chicken) is a classic dish in Szechuan cuisine, originating in the Sichuan Province of central western China. The dish is named after Ding Baozhen (1820\u20131886), a late Qing Dynasty official. Born in Guizhou, Ding served as head of Shandong province and later as governor of Sichuan province. His title was G&#333;ng B&#462;o (&#23470;&#20445;), or palatial guardian. The name \"Kung Pao\" chicken is derived from this title.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 450g (1 lb) [[chicken]], cubed\n| 1 egg white\n| 1 teaspoon [[salt]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[cornflour]]\n| 4 tablespoons [[groundnut oil]]\n| 8 hot [[dried chili peppers]] (or to taste)\n| Handful of [[toasted]] [[cashew nuts]], unsalted if possible\n| 1 small [[onion]], sliced\n| 2 small [[carrots]], [[julienned]] and then chopped\n| 1 teaspoon minced [[Garlic|garlic]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[light soy sauce]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[rice wine]] or [[dry sherry]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[sugar]]\n| 2 teaspoons of [[white wine vinegar]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[sesame oil]]\n| 3 tablespoons of water\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a bowl, mix the egg white, salt and half the [[cornflour]], then coat the cubed chicken pieces with this mixture and leave to [[marinate]] for 30 minutes\n| Heat the oil in a wok and fry the [[onions]] and [[carrots]] for 4 minutes and reserve\n| Fry the chicken until lightly browned then remove from pan\n| Add the [[Garlic|garlic]] and chillies and [[stir-fry]] for 2 minutes\n| Return the [[chicken]], [[onions]] and [[carrots]] to the [[wok]] and add the [[soy sauce]], [[wine]], [[sugar]], [[vinegar]] and [[sesame oil]] and stir-fry for 2 minutes\n| In a saucer, mix the remaining [[cornflour]] and water into a smooth paste\n| Add the paste to the [[wok]] and mix well\n| Simmer, stirring as required, until the sauce clears and the [[chicken]] is properly cooked\n| Add the [[toasted]] [[cashew nuts]] just before serving to ensure they stay crunchy\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Plain rice|plain rice]] or [[egg fried rice]]\n===Chef's notes===\nCarrots and onions may not be authentic, but I like the colour and crunch of the carrots and the taste of the onions.\n\nIf you really don't like crunchy carrots, you may want to [[parboil]] them for a few minutes before you start cooking the dish.\n\n==See also==\n\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]][[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#kungpochicken #chicken #carrots #cornflour #toasted #eggfriedrice #onions #garlic #sesameoil #cashewnuts #wok </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]

odd stuff, and a strange accompaniment to any bovine meat, but it works astonishingly well with it.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:RecipeLamb with oyster sauce Ingredients.jpg|thumb|right|300px|The ingredients]]\nA Szechwan (Szechuan or Sichuan) style lamb dish.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 tablespoons groundnut oil\n| 1 clove [[Garlic|garlic]], crushed\n| 1 slice [[ginger]], finely chopped\n| 450 g (1 lb) lean lamb, cut into &#189;\" thick medallions and flattened under a large knife\n| 250 ml (8 fl oz) [[chicken stock]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[oyster sauce]]\n| 1 tablespoon rice wine or [[dry sherry]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[sugar]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a wok on a medium heat, fry the [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[ginger]] until brown but don't allow it to burn\n| Add the lamb pieces and [[fry]] until [[browned]], about 3 minutes\n| Mix in the stock, [[sherry]], [[oyster sauce]] and [[sugar]] and bring to the boil\n| Cover and simmer for 30 minutes, stirring now and then until the meat is cooked\n| Remove the cover and bring to the boil, stirring continuously to reduce and thicken the sauce\n| Arrange on a serving dish\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe hot with [[rice]] or egg [[noodles]]\n===Variations===\n\nProbably not authentic, but for a bit of colour and extra flavour add a handful of [[cherry tomatoes]] and some sliced [[green peppers]] during the last 10 minutes of cooking.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#lambwithoystersauce #garlic #ginger #oystersauce #fry #panfried #cherrytomatoes #sherry #greenpeppers #browned #chickenstock </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Miso soup, Fish recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#misosoup #tofu #soup #misopaste #simmer #dashi #boil #dashisoupstock #miso #springonions #boiledorsimmered \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Miso soup is a traditional Japanese soup consisting of a stock called \"dashi\" into which is mixed softened miso paste\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2031\n|PortionCalories = 507\n|DatePublished=12th April 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 7 minutes\n |PrepTime = 2 minutes\n |CookTime = 5 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Miso soup recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Strange!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">3</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">..but true.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\n\nMiso soup is a traditional Japanese soup consisting of a stock called \"[[dashi]]\" into which is mixed softened [[miso paste]]. Although the suspension of [[miso paste]] into [[dashi]] is the only characteristic that actually defines miso soup, many other ingredients are added depending on regional and seasonal recipes, and personal preference.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 750 ml (3 cups) [[dashi soup stock]]\n| 1 block [[Tofu|tofu]]\n| 3 tablespoons [[miso paste]]\n| 2 large or 4 small [[Spring onions, chopped|spring onions, chopped]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the [[dashi soup stock]] to a medium sized pan and bring to a [[Boil|boil]].\n| Reduce the heat to a [[Simmer|simmer]], cut the [[Tofu|tofu]] into small cubes and add them to the pan - don't allow the [[Soup|soup]] to [[Boil|boil]] once you have added the [[Tofu|tofu]].\n| [[Simmer]] for a few minutes.\n| Add a few tablespoons of the [[Soup|soup]] to a small bowl add the [[Miso|miso]] paste and stir well to mix the miso.\n| Little by little, add all of the [[Miso|miso]] mix back to the [[Soup|soup]], stirring as you do,.\n| Remove from the heat, add the [[Spring onions|spring onions]], divide into 4 bowls and serve.\n}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#misosoup #tofu #soup #misopaste #simmer #dashi #boil #dashisoupstock #miso #springonions #boiledorsimmered </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Nam phrik kaeng som",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Nam phrik kaeng som recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chilies #shallots #shrimppaste #namphrikkaengsom #fishsauce #pestleandmortar #unusualrecipes #sauce #chili #mortarandpestle #garlic \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Nam Prik Kaeng Som (Thai Sour curry paste) is the base sauce for many Thai curries\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 132\n|PortionCalories = 16\n|DatePublished=27th October 2014\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Nam phrik kapi (foreground)\n|Servings = Servings: 8 - Makes one batch\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime =  13 minutes\n|PrepTime =  10 minutes\n|CookTime =  3 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Nam_phrik_kapi.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Must have Thai fish sauce</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">It's the only way to make this authentic.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nNam Prik Kaeng Som (Thai Sour [[Curry paste|curry paste]])\n\nThis is the base [[Sauce|sauce]] for many Thai [[Curries|curries]].\n\nNam phrik (Thai: \u0e19\u0e49\u0e33\u0e1e\u0e23\u0e34\u0e01, pronounced [n\u00e1m p\u02b0r\u00edk], lit. \"fluid chili\") is a generic term that may refer to any of the types of more or less viscous, spicy, [[chili]]-based, hot sauces typical of [[Thai cuisine]]. Usual ingredients for nam phrik are fresh or dry [[chilies]], [[garlic]], [[shallots]], [[lime juice]] and often some kind of fish or [[shrimp paste]]. In the traditional way of preparing the sauce, the ingredients are pounded together using a [[mortar and pestle]], with either [[salt]] or [[fish sauce]] added to taste.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 10 [[Dried]] [[Chilies|chilies]]\n| 5 [[Shallots]], chopped\n| 1 tablespoon [[Shrimp paste]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Salt]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Coarsely chop the [[Chilies|chilies]] and soak in water for 10 minutes.  Drain.\n| Combine all of the ingredients into a paste, using a [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]]\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nThis sauce goes well with fish and vegetables and is the base for many Thai curries such as [[Thai Moringa curry with shrimp]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n===Reference===\n* [http://www.recipesource.com/ethnic/asia/thai/02/rec0250.html www.recipesource.com/ethnic/asia/thai/02/rec0250.html]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chilies #shallots #shrimppaste #namphrikkaengsom #fishsauce #pestleandmortar #unusualrecipes #sauce #chili #mortarandpestle #garlic </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

[http://www.guardian.co.uk/lifeandstyle/wordofmouth/2009/may/14/ghent-vegetarian-city-healthy-belgium Gent night] recipes.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 450 g (1 lb) fresh or [[Dried|dried]] Chinese [[Egg noodles|egg noodles]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Sesame oil|sesame oil]]\n| 450 g (1lb) [[Cucumber|cucumber]] (one [[cucumber]])\n| 175 g (6 oz) fresh [[Bean sprouts|bean sprouts]]\n}}\n'''Dressing'''\n* 1 tablespoon [[Garlic]], peeled and crushed\n* 1 tablespoon [[Ginger root|ginger root]], peeled and very finely chopped or [[Grated|grated]]\n* 2 teaspoons [[Light soy sauce|light soy sauce]]\n* 1 tablespoon [[Dark soy sauce|dark soy sauce]]\n* 1 tablespoon [[Sugar|sugar]] ( I prefer [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]])\n* 2.5 tablespoons [[Sesame paste|sesame paste]] ([[Tahini|tahini]])\n* 1 tablespoon [[White wine vinegar|white wine vinegar]]\n* 2 teaspoons [[Chilli oil|chilli oil]]\n'''To serve'''\n* 1 teaspoon [[Granulated sugar|granulated sugar]]\n* 3 tablespoons [[Sesame seeds|sesame seeds]], lightly [[Toasted|toasted]]\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Cook the [[Noodles|noodles]] as instructed, refresh under cold water, rinse and drain then toss in the [[Sesame oil|sesame oil]]\n| Peel the [[Cucumbers|cucumbers]], cut into 4 length-ways and run your knife down the 'triangle' to remove and discard the [[Seeds|seeds]].\n| Cut into thin slices ([[Food processor|food processor]] is your friend here)\n| [[Blanche]] the [[Bean sprouts|bean sprouts]] in [[Boiling|boiling]] water for 1 minute then rinse and drain in cold water\n| Mix the dressing ingredients well, add the [[Noodles|noodles]] and [[Cucumbers|cucumbers]] and toss in the dressing\n| Sprinkle with [[Sugar|sugar]] and [[Sesame seeds|sesame seeds]] and serve immediately\n}}\n===Chef's note===\nIf using [[Very lazy ginger]] or the [[Very lazy ginger#How to Make your own lazy ginger|homemade version of the same thing]], use the vinegar from that instead of [[white wine vinegar]].\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Pasta recipes]]\n[[Category:Pasta salad title": "Oriental sous vide silverside beef",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Oriental sous vide silverside beef recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#beef #szechuanpeppercorns #orientalsousvidesilversidebeef #vacuumsealer #marinade #fineyellowcornmeal #lightsoysauce #shoyo #pestleandmortar #shoyubeef #fat \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This recipe is similar to Shoyu beef, which is distinctly Japanese. I thought I would try a similar recipe using sous vide cooking and using everyday\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2350\n|PortionCalories = 1175\n|DatePublished=16th February 2015\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 2 with leftovers!\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  12 hours, 15 minutes\n|PrepTime =  15 minutes\n|CookTime =  12 hours\n|Image = [[Image:Oriental sous vide silverside beef recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Slice it thin!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This was much nicer when we cut it thin with a proper meat slicer.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Sous vide silverside.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Silverside joint sealed ready for the sous vide oven]]\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n\nThis recipe is similar to [[Shoyu beef]], which is distinctly Japanese.  I thought I would try a similar recipe using sous vide cooking and using everyday ingredients as some of the Japanese ingredients can be difficult to find.  I also wanted to experiment with this sous vide recipe using relatively  economic silverside of [[Beef|beef]] rather than beef fillet.\n\nI've used Chardonnay instead of [[Mirin]], not a great substitute but I always have some Chardonnay in the freezer in paper cups.  Dead easy to scoop a spoonful out when needed for cooking, and it saves having to drink the dreadful stuff! [[Light soy sauce|light soy sauce]] is pretty close to [[shoyo]].  I use [[Frozen ginger paste]] which is almost as good as the real thing.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 700g [1lb 8 oz] [[Beef|beef]] silverside joint, trimmed of excess [[Fat|fat]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[White wine|white wine]]\n| 2 tablespoons of [[Light soy sauce|light soy sauce]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Grated|grated]] [[Ginger|ginger]] (thumb sized piece of ginger, peeled and grated)\n| 1/4 of a teaspoon [[Szechuan peppercorns|szechuan peppercorns]] crushed in a [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]]\n| 1 tablespoon of [[fine yellow cornmeal]] to thicken the gravy, optional.\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Stamp the joint all over with a [[meat tenderiser]] tool. This helps to tenderize the joint and also allow the [[Marinade|marinade]] to permeate the meat.\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| When selecting the size of pouch to contain the [[Beef|beef]], make one that is quite a bit larger than the joint.  This seems to make it easier to seal without drawing all the [[Marinade|marinade]] into the [[Vacuum sealer|vacuum sealer]].\n| Being careful not to wet the inner edges of the bag where it will be sealed, add all of the ingredients, apart from the cornmeal to the vacuum bag.\n| Set the [[Vacuum sealer|vacuum sealer]] so the bag can hang vertically over the edge of the work surface.\n| Press the [[Vacuum seal|vacuum seal]] button on your sealer and then cancel just as any liquid begins to be drawn into the sealing chamber.  Then press heat seal to seal the bag.  The pessimist in me always seals the bag a couple of times at each end, just in case!\n| Sous vide cook at 68\u00b0C (''154.4\u00b0F'') for 12 hours for medium - well done.  See [[Sous vide cooking times]] for other levels of doneness.\n| If you want to thicken the gravy, immediately the 12 hours cooking is complete, add the juices to a hot pan together with a tablespoon of [[fine yellow cornmeal]], bring to a simmer, stirring all the while.\n| Carve and serve.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Potatoes|potatoes]] and a [[Vegetable|vegetable]] of your choice.\n===Chef's notes===\nThis was fantastic, the meat was so tender and juicy that it didn't really need any gravy.  I've now reduced the quantity of the [[szechuan peppercorns]] as they were a little overpowering.  Any strong flavours multiply when cooking in a vac packed bag.\n\nI've not found any benefit to resting meat when cooking [[sous vide]] and in this instance I did not sear the outside of the meat as it looked great with all the peppercorns around the edge.\n{{SousVideSeeAlso}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Sous vide recipes]]\n[[Category:Sous vide cooking]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#beef #szechuanpeppercorns #orientalsousvidesilversidebeef #vacuumsealer #marinade #fineyellowcornmeal #lightsoysauce #shoyo #pestleandmortar #shoyubeef #fat </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
