Serve as a starter with finger bowls and napkins or as a main course with plain boiled rice. \n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2660\n|PortionCalories = 665\n|DatePublished=21st January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 hour 40 minutes\n |PrepTime = 1 hour 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 30 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Sweet and sour spare ribs recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Nice with fillet slices</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.6</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Though very different to actaul ribs</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n\nA simple and tasty way to serve economic [[Spare ribs|spare ribs]].  Serve as a [[Starter|starter]] with finger bowls and napkins or as a [[Main course|main course]] with [[Plain boiled rice|plain boiled rice]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 675 g (1.5 lb) spare rib chops or [[Pork fillet|escalopes of pork tenderloin fillet]]\n| Juice of 1 [[lemon]] or [[lime]].\n| 2  tablespoons [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]]\n| &frac12;  cup of water\n| &frac14;  cup [[Jaggery|jaggery]] or [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]] \t \n| 2  tablespoons [[Cornflour|cornflour]]\n| 1  teaspoon [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] \t \n| 2 teaspoons of [[Szechuan peppercorns]]\n| 1 dried red chili, crushed.\n| &frac14;  cup [[Vinegar|vinegar]] of your choice. [[Chinese black vinegar]] is nice with this.\n| 2 tablespoons [[Light soy sauce|light soy sauce]] \t \n| &frac34;  cup [[Sweet peppers|sweet peppers]], deseeded and chopped (any colours)\n| &frac14;  cup [[Onion|onion]], peeled and finely chopped\n| 1  cup [[Pineapple|pineapple]] [[Juice|juice]] \t \n| 1 cup [[Pineapple|pineapple]] chunks\n|* 1 medium can of pineapple chunks will provide enough juice and chunks for this dish.\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Cut the [[Ribs|ribs]] into individual chops, if they are long, cut them in half lengthwise too.\n| Marinade the ribs or escalopes of pork tenderloin fillet in lemon juice, 1 teaspoon of crushed Szechuan peppercorns and a little salt for an hour or so to tenderise.\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a [[Wok|wok]] and [[Brown|brown]] the [[Ribs|ribs]] for 4 minutes, turning often.\n| Add the water and [[Vinegar|vinegar]], the remaining teaspoon of crushed Szechuan peppercorns, the crushed chili and bring to the [[Boil|boil]] and [[Simmer|simmer]] until properly cooked (about 10 to 15 minutes) - just 5 minutes if using thin fillet.\n| Remove the [[Ribs|ribs]] set to one side, leaving a little liquid/oil in the [[Wok|wok]].\n| Add the onions and peppers and [[Saut\u00e9e|saut\u00e9e]] for a few minutes.\n| Pre-mix the [[Cornflour|cornflour]] in a little cold water.\n| Add the [[Pineapple|pineapple]] [[Juice|juice]], [[Salt|salt]], [[Jaggery|jaggery]], [[Soy sauce|soy sauce]] to the [[Wok|wok]], stir in the [[Cornflour|cornflour]] and mix well.\n| Cook for 5 minutes, stirring often as the mixture thickens.\n| Add the [[Ribs|ribs]] back to the [[Wok|wok]] together with the [[Pineapple|pineapple]] chunks and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 5 minutes.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe hot with [[Plain boiled rice|plain boiled rice]] or [[Noodles|noodles]].\n===Variations===\nMade this with [[Pork fillet|escalopes of pork tenderloin fillet]] in place of the spare-ribs as they were on special offer.\n\nSome fresh green vegetables, such as peas would have been nice, added at the very end to contrast with the highly flavoured sauce.\n===Chef's notes===\n{{Template:ThinkPig}}\n==See also==\n* [[Sweet and sour recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pineapple #wok #ribs #cornflour #juice #sweetandsourspareribs #plainboiledrice #simmer #vinegar #jaggery #boiledorsimmered </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

After the steaming is finished, let the pork [[Rest for|rest for]] about 10 minutes.\n| Cut and slice the [[Pork|pork]] into pieces.\n| Put the [[Palm sugar|palm sugar]] into the pan then stir it over a low heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] until the colour of the [[Sugar|sugar]] is [[Brown|brown]].\n| Add [[Fish sauce|fish sauce]] and water all together then add the [[Pork|pork]] and mix them.\n| Finally, you must [[Simmer|simmer]] it for about 5-10 minutes then mix the [[Pork|pork]] and the [[Sauce|sauce]] together\n}}\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Marinades dressings and butters]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Steamed]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pork #sweetporkcondiment #rice #simmer #palmsugar #lightsoysauce #fishsauce #refrigerator #fried #steam #bellyofpork </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Szechuan hot chili pork",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Szechuan hot chili pork, Meat recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#szechuanhotchilipork #cornflour #sesameoil #garlic #springonions #lightsoysauce #redchillies #eggs #deepfried \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This is one of those dishes that is better than the restaurant version, especially because you can tinker with it to get the taste exactly as you like\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1851\n|PortionCalories = 462\n|DatePublished=31st January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 35 minutes\n|PrepTime = 15 minutes\n|CookTime = 20 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:RecipeSzechuan hot chili pork.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Pork as it should be</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Nice and spicy</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Carla_Cancio-Bello,_J.D.,_on_behalf_of_Cuban_Cuisine_UK|Carla]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis is one of those dishes that is better than the restaurant version, especially because you can tinker with it to get the taste exactly as you like it.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 large [[eggs]]\n| 4 tablespoons [[cornflour]]\n| 1 lb pork (loin, leg or shoulder)\n| Oil for deep-frying\n| 2 carrots\n| 2 [[Garlic|garlic]] cloves, crushed\n| 2 fresh [[red chillies]]\n| 2 [[spring onions]] (scallions)\n| 2 tablespoons white wine vinegar\n| 1 tablespoon [[light soy sauce]]\n| 1 teaspoon sea [[salt]]\n| 4 tablespoons [[sugar]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[sesame oil]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Cut the meat into thin slices\n| Peel the carrots and cut into thin slices\n| Mix the eggs and [[cornflour]] into a paste, stir the meat into this mixture and ensure it's well coated\n| Heat the oil for deep-frying in a wok or deep saucepan until a cube of bread browns within 15 seconds\n| Add the meat in batches and fry for 4-5 minutes. Remove and keep warm. Repeat until all meat is cooked\n| Add the carrots to the oil and fry for 3 minutes\n| This may cause the oil to froth over so do this in batches and be very careful - remove and drain on kitchen paper\n| Carefully drain the oil from the wok, leave 1 tablespoon oil in the bottom. Alternatively use another pan\n| Add [[Garlic|garlic]] and spring onions and fry for 1 minute\n| Add vinegar, soy sauce, sugar and [[salt]]. Mix well and add the cooked meat and carrots to the sauce\n| Arrange on a serving dish, sprinkle with [[sesame oil]] and serve hot\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\n{{Template:ThinkPig}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Pork]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine|Pork]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Pork]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Pork]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Deep fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#szechuanhotchilipork #cornflour #sesameoil #garlic #springonions #lightsoysauce #redchillies #eggs #deepfried </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Inspired by a lovely soup they had in a Japanese restaurant in Kensington\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|DatePublished=29th September 2016\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = 2\n|Difficulty = 3\n|TotalTime = 1 day, 1 hour\n|PrepTime = 1 day, 15 minutes\n|CookTime =  45 minutes\n|TotalCalories = 3581\n|PortionCalories = 1790\n|Image = [[Image:Tantan soup with ramen, pak choi and mad eggs recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Wicked!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.9</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Love your mad eggs!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The&nbsp;Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis recipe comes to [[Cookipedia]] by courtesy of [[Nik and Edwina's Cookbook]].\n\n\"Inspired by a lovely [[Soup|soup]] we had in a Japanese restaurant in Kensington, this is a deliciously comforting, nutty flavoured soup, with the [[Noodles|noodles]] and [[Pak choi|pak choi]] and particularly the [[Eggs|eggs]] providing a rich and tasty counterpoint. If you [[Freeze|freeze]] the soup it can separate a bit, so give it a quick whizz in a [[Blender|blender]] when you [[Defrost|defrost]] it\"\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n}}\n====The Mad Eggs:- ====\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 200ml regular [[Soy sauce|soy sauce]]&#8232; \n| 200ml water&#8232; \n| 20g [[Sugar|sugar]] \n| \u00bd teaspoons [[Truffle oil|truffle oil]]\n| 4 whole [[Soft-boiled eggs|soft-boiled eggs]], carefully peeled \n}}\n====The Tantan Soup:- ====\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 750ml [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]] \n| 375ml [[Nage]]\n| 250ml [[Dashi]]\n| 100g white [[Sesame seeds|sesame seeds]] &#8232; \n| 150g [[Tahini|tahini]] \n| 100mls regular [[Soy sauce|soy sauce]]&#8232; \n| 25g [[Sugar|sugar]]&#8232; \n| 1 hot [[Chilli|chilli]], deseeded and finely chopped \n| 20g [[Ginger|ginger]], peeled and finely chopped&#8232; \n| 15g [[Spring onion|spring onion]], finely chopped&#8232; \n}}\n====To Serve:- ====\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 350g fresh ramen [[Noodles|noodles]] (or use another [[Noodle|noodle]])&#8232; \n| 4 medium sized heads of [[Pak choi|pak choi]], quartered\n| 1 tablespoon finely chopped [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Mix together the [[Soy|soy]], water, [[Sugar|sugar]], and [[Truffle oil|truffle oil]], then [[Marinate|marinate]] the [[Eggs|eggs]] in this overnight if possible, but for at least four hours \n| Heat a [[Frying pan|frying pan]], and add the [[Sesame seeds|sesame seeds]], [[Toasting|toasting]] them till a good third of them are [[Browning|browning]] and [[Oil|oil]] is starting to leak from them. Whizz them in a [[Blender|blender]]\n| Put the [[Stocks|stocks]] in a good sized heavy bottomed pan, bring them to a [[Boil|boil]]. Whisk in the [[Sesame|sesame]] mix,  then add the [[Soy|soy]], the [[Sugar|sugar]], the [[Chilli|chilli]], the [[Ginger|ginger]], the [[Spring onions|spring onions]] and the [[Tahini|tahini]].\n| Bring back to a [[Boil|boil]] and [[Simmer|simmer]] gently for 15 mins. Whisk the [[Dashi|dashi]] in, bring back to the boil again, then take off the heat.\n| Meanwhile, [[Steam|steam]] the [[Pak choy|pak choy]] till it\u0092s only just done, and set aside, then cook your [[Noodles|noodles]].\n| Place a quarter of the [[Noodles|noodles]] in each of four deep [[Soup|soup]] bowls, and ladle a portion of soup into each. [[Pile]] some [[Pak choi|pak choi]] on top.\n| Place a [[Soft boiled egg|soft boiled egg]] on top of the [[Pak choi|pak choi]], sprinkle with the chopped [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]] and serve\n}}\n===Recipe source===\n\n* https://sites.google.com/site/nikandedwinascookbook/Home/soups/tantan-soup-with-ramen-pak-choi-and-mad-eggs\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Egg recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Nik and Edwina's Cookbook recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#noodles #pakchoi #tantansoupwithramenpakchoiandmadeggs #soy #boil #ginger #tahini #corianderleaves #dashi #truffleoil #blender </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Tempura batter recipe",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Tempura batter recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#cornflour #plainflour #sparklingwater #flour #tempurabatterrecipe #deepfried #eggs #balloonwhisk #deepfatfryer #bakingsoda #lager \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=A recipe for a light batter made of cold sparkling water which is used to keep the batter light\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 826\n|PortionCalories = 206\n|DatePublished=10th November 2014\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = Tempura vegetables\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 3\n |TotalTime = 30 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 15 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Tempura vegetables.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Tricksey!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Delicious, but I find it hard to make it stick to the food.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]])</span></span>\n}}\n===Tempura batter===\nA light batter is made of cold water (sometimes [[sparkling water]] is used to keep the batter light) and [[plain flour]] (''all purpose flour''). [[Eggs]], [[baking soda]] or [[baking powder]], [[cornflour|starch]], [[oil]], and spices may also be added.\n\nTempura batter is traditionally mixed in small batches using chopsticks for only a few seconds, leaving lumps in the mixture that, along with the cold batter temperature, result in the unique fluffy and crisp tempura structure when cooked. The batter is often kept cold by adding ice, or by placing the bowl inside a larger bowl with ice in it. \n\n'''Over mixing the batter will result in activation of wheat gluten, which causes the flour mixture to become chewy and dough-like when fried.'''\n===Origins===\nThe recipe for tempura was introduced to Japan by Portuguese Jesuit missionaries particularly active in the city of Nagasaki also founded by the Portuguese, during the sixteenth century (1549).\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 75g [[Plain flour|plain flour]]\n| 75g [[Corn flour|cornflour]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| 188 ml [6.5 fl oz] [[sparkling water]], [[beer]] or [[lager]].  Must be ice cold.\n| 1 free range egg - lightly beaten\n| [[Plain flour]] for dredging\n|[[Vegetable oil]] for deep frying\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in either a [[Deep fat fryer|deep fat fryer]] or a large saucepan. If you are using a saucepan make sure the oil comes below halfway down the edge of the pan. If you have a [[Thermometer|thermometer]] it needs to reach 190C, but you can test that it\u0092s ready by dropping some [[Bread|bread]] into the oil and it should [[Brown|brown]] in 20 seconds.\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Ensure the water is ice cold.\n| Sift the [[flour]], [[cornflour]] and [[salt]] together into a bowl. \n| Make a well in the centre of the flour and pour your chosen liquid together with the previously beaten egg into it.\n| Using a [[balloon whisk]], very gently combine ingredients into a rough batter.\n| It is very important that it is not overmixed at this stage as that will make the batter stodgy.\n| Once your batter is 'runny' enough to coat your chosen filling, stop mixing, even if this leaves the odd lump in the batter.  \n| Dredge your filling through the plain flour to coat well and then dip into the batter and deep fry for 2 to 3 minutes in small batches.\n| Cooked tempura can be kept warm in an oven at 150\u00b0 C (300\u00b0 F), with the door left ajar to keep it crispy.\n}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:British Onions recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:Deep fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#cornflour #plainflour #sparklingwater #flour #tempurabatterrecipe #deepfried #eggs #balloonwhisk #deepfatfryer #bakingsoda #lager </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }
}

teaspoon [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| 200ml ice cold sparkling water\n| 300ml [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]]\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], sliced into rings, each ring separated into 2 ring thickness\n| 1 [[Red onion|red onion]] sliced into rings, each ring separated into 2 ring thickness\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oven|oven]] to 150\u00b0 C (300\u00b0 F - gas 2).\n| Mix together the [[Sauce|sauce]] ingredients and set aside. You also need to ensure that the water is ice cold. Add some ice cubes into if you'\u0092re worried it\u0092s not up to temperature. \n| Line a [[Baking tray|baking tray]] with [[Greaseproof paper|greaseproof paper]].\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in either a [[Deep fat fryer|deep fat fryer]] or a large saucepan. If you are using a saucepan make sure the oil comes below halfway down the edge of the pan. If you have a [[Thermometer|thermometer]] it needs to reach 190C, but you can test that it\u0092s ready by dropping some [[Bread|bread]] into the oil and it should [[Brown|brown]] in 20 seconds.\n| [[Dip]] a third of the [[Onions|onions]] into the [[Batter|batter]] shaking off any excess and [[Fry|fry]] for 2 minutes until golden and crisp. \n| Remove the [[Onions|onions]] with a [[Slotted spoon|slotted spoon]] and drain. \n| Place them onto the [[Baking|baking]] sheet and repeat with the rest of the [[Onions|onions]]. It is important you [[Fry|fry]] them in batches to ensure they get really crisp. While each batch is cooking, keep the others warm in the [[Oven|oven]], but leave the door open to keep them crisp\n| Serve the tempura [[Onions|onions]] with the gingery dipping [[Sauce|sauce]].\n}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:British Onions recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:Deep fried]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n{{Template:British Onions attribution}}\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#onions #tempuraonionsrings #sauce #fry #cornflour #onion #grated #rice #plainflour #unusualrecipes #slottedspoon </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Thai chicken with coconut and lime",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Thai chicken with coconut and lime Cooking with chillies recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chicken #thaichickenwithcoconutandlime #currypaste #springonions #limejuice #zest #corianderleaves #nampla #plainboiledrice #boil #greencurrypaste \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This Thai-style dish is a mild curry - you could spice this up just by adding a few teaspoons of good quality curry paste - I recommend the Cock brand\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 3605\n|PortionCalories = 1802\n|DatePublished=31st October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Coconut, chicken!\n |Servings = Serves 2\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 1 hour 20 minutes\n |PrepTime = 1 hour 5 minutes\n |CookTime = 15 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Thai chicken with coconut and lime recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">I LOVE the photo for this recipe</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Absolute genius!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:NonLoggedInUser|NonLoggedInUser]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis Thai-style dish is a mild curry - you could spice this up just by adding a few teaspoons of good quality [[curry paste]] - I recommend the [[Curry paste|Cock brand]] if you can get it. Use what you need for the recipe and freeze the rest, you can spoon it directly from the freezer as you need it.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 400 g skinless [[Chicken|chicken]] breasts cut into bite-sized chunks of equal size.\n| [[Juice]] and freshly [[Grated|grated]] [[Zest|zest]] of 2 [[Limes|limes]].\n| 1 can [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Peanut oil|peanut oil]]\n| 2 green chillies, finely chopped or 2 teaspoons of [[green curry paste]]\n| 1 tablespoon of [[Jaggery|jaggery]] or [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Nam pla|nam pla]]\n| 1 [[Spring onion|spring onion]], [[Chopped on the diagonal|chopped on the diagonal]]\n}}\n'''garnish'''\n* Freshly chopped [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]]\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the [[Lime juice|lime juice]] and [[Zest|zest]] to a bowl with the [[Chicken|chicken]], mix well and [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] for at least 1 hour, longer if you have time.\n| Drain the [[Lime juice|lime juice]] from the [[Chicken|chicken]] and reserve for later.\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a [[Wok|wok]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] the [[Chicken|chicken]] until it's nicely [[Browned|browned]] - about 3 or 4 minutes on a high heat.\n| Add the [[Chillies|chillies]] or [[Curry paste|curry paste]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] for a few minutes, mixing well.\n| Add the [[Coconut|coconut]], [[Lime|lime]], [[Nam pla|nam pla]], [[Sugar|sugar]], half of the [[Spring onions|spring onions]] and half of the [[Coriander|coriander]], just bring it to the [[Boil|boil]], reduce the heat immediately and [[Simmer|simmer]] for a few minutes until the [[Chicken|chicken]] is properly cooked.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nSprinkle with the remaining chopped [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]] and [[Spring onions|spring onions]] and serve with [[Plain boiled rice|plain boiled rice]] or [[egg noodles]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]]\n[[Category:Thai recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #thaichickenwithcoconutandlime #currypaste #springonions #limejuice #zest #corianderleaves #nampla #plainboiledrice #boil #greencurrypaste </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Thai Melon Soup recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#coconutmilk #lemongrass #melon #ginger #chilli #zest #thaimelonsoup #mint #foodprocessor #basil #blender \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This soup is ridiculously refreshing and outrageously delicious. The perfect light summer lunch or starter\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1940\n|PortionCalories = 485\n|DatePublished=16th August 2014\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  15 minutes\n|PrepTime =  15 minutes\n|CookTime = None\n|Image = [[Image:Thai Melon Soup recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Melon \ud83c\udf48 soup \ud83c\udf72</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.2</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Fresh and clean, with that lovely aroma of basil.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis [[Soup|soup]] is ridiculously refreshing and outrageously delicious. The perfect light summer [[Lunch|lunch]] or [[Starter|starter]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 ripe Galia or Honeydew [[Melon|melon]]\n| 1 [[Cucumber|cucumber]]\n| 1 stalk of [[Lemongrass|lemongrass]]\n| 1 heaped teaspoon of freshly [[Grated|grated]] [[Ginger|ginger]]\n| A good pinch of finely chopped fresh [[Chilli|chilli]] (more or less to taste)\n| 200ml [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]]\n| A large handful of Thai or regular [[Basil|basil]]\n| A small handful of fresh [[Mint|mint]]\n| 1-2 [[Limes|limes]], [[Juice|juice]] and [[Zest|zest]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Halve your [[Melon|melon]]. [[Scoop]] out the [[Seeds|seeds]]. Spoon the flesh from the skin straight into a [[Blender|blender]] or [[Food processor|food processor]].\n| Peel your [[Cucumber|cucumber]]. Roughly chop. Add to the [[Melon|melon]].\n| Bash your [[Lemongrass|lemongrass]] stalk till it flattens and softens a bit. Peel the outer layer away. Thinly slice starting at the base. Finely chop till you have about 1 heaped tsp.\n| Add the [[Lemongrass|lemongrass]] to the [[Blender|blender]]/[[Food processor|food processor]] along with the [[Ginger|ginger]], [[Chilli|chilli]], [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]], [[Basil|basil]], [[Mint|mint]] and the [[Zest|zest]] and [[Juice|juice]] of 1 [[Lime|lime]].\n| Whizz till smooth. Taste. Add more [[Lemongrass|lemongrass]], [[Ginger|ginger]], [[Chilli|chilli]], [[Herbs|herbs]] or [[Lime juice|lime juice]] as needed. Swirl in a bit more [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]], too, if needed (depends on the [[Melon|melon]]\u0092s sweetness).\n| Once it's so good you can't stop eating it, pop it in the [[Freezer|freezer]] to chill quickly or the [[Fridge|fridge]] if you\u0092re serving it later. Lovely garnished with a swirl of [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] drizzled on top and some fresh [[Basil leaves|basil leaves]].\n}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Vietnamese recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Abel and Cole veg box recipes]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n{{Template:Abel and Cole veg box recipes attribution}}\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:Thai recipes]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#coconutmilk #lemongrass #melon #ginger #chilli #zest #thaimelonsoup #mint #foodprocessor #basil #blender </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Sorry.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kaeng_som Kaeng Som] Puk Marum or Thai Moringa [[Curry|curry]] with [[Shrimp|shrimp]] has a spicy and sour shrimp curry taste or [[Soup|soup]] with moringa  popular in central of Thailand.\n[[Nam phrik kaeng som]] is prepared as a base for the [[Curry|curry]], then water and the other [[Ingredient|ingredient]]s are added ,but the main ingredient is moringa. For the preparation of Thai moringa curry the [[Shrimp|shrimp]] and [[Shallots|shallots]] and all of the ingredients are pound with a [[Mortar and pestle|mortar and pestle]]. \n\n[[Shrimp]] or [[Fish|fish]] may be used as the basic [[Ingredient|ingredient]]. Thai [[moringa]] [[Curry|curry]] with shrimp is usually served with [[Steamed rice|steamed rice]]. \n\nThe [[Curry|curry]] has sour taste, which comes from ripe [[Tamarind|tamarind]] and uses [[Palm sugar|palm sugar]] for sweeten the curry taste.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 800g [[Moringa]]\t\t\n| 40g [[Shrimp]] or [[Fish|fish]]\t\t\t\n| 1g Nam Phrik Kaeng Som\t\n| \u00bc Ripe [[Tamarind|tamarind]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Palm sugar]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Fish sauce]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Peel the [[moringa]], and clean them then cut into the pieces , of about three inches length\n| Bring water to a rapid [[Boil|boil]], add [[Shrimp|shrimp]] and boil until cooked, then remove the [[Shrimps|shrimps]] and cool down. Keep the [[Stock|stock]] for the [[Soup|soup]] base.\n| In the mortar, take 2-3 whole [[Shrimps|shrimps]], and pounded together with [[Nam Phrik Kaeng Som]] until thoroughly mixed.\n| Bring the [[Nam Phrik Kaeng Som]] that was pounded with [[Shrimp|shrimp]] to the [[Boil|boil]] and [[Simmer|simmer]] over a high heat for 5 minutes.\n| Add the [[moringa]] and season with [[Palm sugar|palm sugar]], [[Fish sauce|fish sauce]], and concentrated [[Tamarind|tamarind]] [[Juice|juice]] and bring to the [[Boil|boil]]. Add the [[Rest|rest]] of [[Shrimps|shrimps]] and, when it boils again turn off the heat.\n| Serve.\n}}\n===Recipe source===\n* Recipe text by [[User:Nutcha Waropashpimarn]]\n==See also==\n\n* http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kaeng_som\n* [http://www.recipesource.com/ethnic/asia/thai/02/rec0250.html Nam Phrik Kaeng Som]\n* [http://www.doctor.or.th/article/detail/1053 www.doctor.or.th/article/detail/1053]\n* http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moringa\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Vietnamese recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Freshwater fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Thai recipes]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#shrimp #curry #moringa #tamarind #palmsugar #boil #shrimps #thaimoringacurrywithshrimp #soup #fish #fishsauce </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Thanks Panrapee</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Looks like a fabulous way to serve oysters - can't wait to try this at home.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nThai [[Fried|fried]] [[Oysters|oysters]] (Thai : &#3627;&#3629;&#3618;&#3607;&#3629;&#3604;(Hoii-thot), [[Chinese]] : &#3629;&#3629;&#3626;&#3656;&#3623;&#3609;(Or-Suan)) is a famous fast food in Thailand that you can find on many street corners in Bangkok and also popular in other places such as Taiwan, Hong Kong, and the Philippines. The main ingredients are [[Flour|flour]], [[Spice|spice]], [[Egg|egg]], and [[Oyster|oyster]] serve with [[Bean sprouts|bean sprouts]] and [[Chilli sauce|chilli sauce]] on the hot plate. This food is very popular because there are five categories of nutrients.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 10 small [[Oysters|oysters]] (or [[Mussels|mussels]], [[Squid|squid]], or [[Seafood|seafood]] as you prefer)\n| 2 tablespoons [[Rice flour|rice flour]]\n| &#189; tablespoon [[Cassava|cassava]] [[Starch|starch]] \n| 1 cup fresh [[Bean sprouts|bean sprouts]]\n| 3 tablespoons cold water\n| &#188; teaspoon Thai [[Pepper powder|pepper powder]]\n| &#188; teaspoon chopped [[Garlic|garlic]]\n| &#188; teaspoon chopped [[Onion|onion]]\n| &#188; teaspoon [[Fish sauce|fish sauce]]\n| 1 [[free range egg]]\n| [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]] for cooking\n}}\n'''[[Chilli sauce|chilli sauce]] for [[Oysters|oysters]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 2 tablespoons sweet [[Chilli sauce|chilli sauce]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Vinegar|vinegar]]\n| &#188; teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Wash [[Oysters|oysters]] in cold water, then [[Poached|poached]] and drain well.\n| Mix [[Cassava|cassava]] [[Starch|starch]] and [[Rice flour|rice flour]] with the water and mix well.\n| Heat the [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]] in a pan. When the [[Oil|oil]] is hot, pour the mixed [[Flour|flour]] and [[Oysters|oysters]] together.\n| Add the [[Egg|egg]] after [[Batter|batter]] is set. Make a hole in the centre with a spatula, cook until golden crispy.\n| Pour a little more [[Oil|oil]] in the pan, [[Fry|fry]] the [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Bean sprouts|bean sprouts]] until it heated.\n| Mix all ingredients, then season with [[Fish sauce|fish sauce]], [[Sugar|sugar]], [[Onion|onion]] and Thai [[Pepper powder|pepper powder]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe it with a [[Chilli sauce|chilli sauce]].\n==See also==\n\n* http://pantip.com/topic/30652509, &#3627;&#3629;&#3618;&#3607;&#3629;&#3604;&#3649;&#3611;&#3657;&#3591;&#3585;&#3619;&#3629;&#3610; &#3626;&#3641;&#3605;&#3619;&#3629;&#3619;&#3656;&#3629;&#3618;&#3648;&#3627;&#3634;&#3632; (&#3610;&#3656;&#3591;&#3610;&#3658;&#3591;, June 26, 2014)\n* http://www.pim.in.th/one-dish-food/56-sea-[[Mussel|mussel]]-[[Fried|fried]].html, &#3627;&#3629;&#3618;&#3607;&#3629;&#3604; (&#3614;&#3636;&#3617; @ &#3588;&#3619;&#3633;&#3623;&#3610;&#3657;&#3634;&#3609;&#3614;&#3636;&#3617;, July 17, 2009)\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Vietnamese recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Shellfish recipes]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]]\n[[Category:Thai recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#oysters #chillisauce #beansprouts #pepperpowder #onion #riceflour #cassava #fishsauce #vegetableoil #fried #starch </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Thai sweet sticky rice",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Thai sweet sticky rice recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#rice #coconutmilk #steam #thaisweetstickyrice #pandanus #steamed #mango #ricepudding #steaming #dessert #thairecipes \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Thai sweet sticky rice (Khao Nieaw Moon) has been a popular Thai dessert for many centuries. This is the recipe. \n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4498\n|PortionCalories = 1124\n|DatePublished=24th October 2014\n|Author=Panrapee Satienpisarn\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = 4\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime = 1 day, 1 hour\n|PrepTime = 1 day\n|CookTime =  1 hour\n|Image = [[Image:Wewe recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Authentic!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Sure is sweet and sticky!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Thai sweet sticky rice]] - Thai [[Steamed]] Sticky [[Rice]] with [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] (Khao Nieaw Moon) has been a popular Thai [[Dessert|dessert]] for many centuries. Sweet sticky rice is different from Sticky rice which is non-flavored. It has a few easy steps. When finished, you can just eat sweet sticky rice, but many Thai [[Fruits|fruits]] and [[Desserts|desserts]] can be eaten with sweet sticky rice such as, eat with [[Mangoes|mangoes]], [[Egg custard|egg custard]] (Sang Kha Ya), and durian. All of these are very popular for foreigners.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| &#189; kg. Kieaw Ngu sticky [[Rice|rice]] (soak in water 1 night) \n| 3 Tsp. [[salt]]\n| 400 grams [[sugar]]\n| 500 grams [[Coconut milk]]\n| 3 [[Pandanus]] leaf\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Soak the [[Rice|rice]] in water overnight\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Soak the [[Rice|rice]] in one cup water for 20-30 minutes. Then rinse with clean water 1 time.\n| Place a white cloth in a [[Steaming|steaming]] pot. And [[Steam|steam]] sticky [[Rice|rice]] for 40 minutes until cooked.\n| After 30 minutes has passed, add [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]], [[Sugar|sugar]], [[Salt|salt]], and [[Pandanus|pandanus]] leaves into the pot. Then [[Boil|boil]] for 10 minutes.\n| When 40 minutes has passed, add sticky [[Rice|rice]] into the pot. Follow with [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] and stir to combine. [[Steam]] for 10 minutes.\n| Stir sticky [[Rice|rice]] again. Mix thoroughly and [[Steam|steam]] more for 10 minutes.\n| Top with [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] before serving. Ready to eat.\n}}\n==See also==\n\n* Kasma Loha-unchit (1995), [[Pandanus]] Leaf \u0096Bai Dteuy http://www.thaifoodandtravel.com/ingredients/pandan.html \n* Chef Lek (2012), &#3586;&#3657;&#3634;&#3623;&#3648;&#3627;&#3609;&#3637;&#3618;&#3623;&#3617;&#3641;&#3609; , http://www.foodtravel.tv/recfoodShow_Detail.aspx?viewId=496\n* Darlene Schmidt, Classic Thai [[Mango]] Sticky [[Rice pudding|rice pudding]] (Khao Niaow Ma Muang) http://thaifood.about.com/od/thaidesserts/r/mangoricepuddin.htm\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Vietnamese recipes]]\n[[Category:Sweets and desserts]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Thai recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#rice #coconutmilk #steam #thaisweetstickyrice #pandanus #steamed #mango #ricepudding #steaming #dessert #thairecipes </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }

Hers was an adapted version of [http://www.bbq-nl.com/2009/07/the-renowned-mr-brown.html the original] (''Dutch'').  I have further adapted [http://www.flickr.com/photos/fotoosvanrobin/6308694585/ hers].\n\nThe [[Meat|meat]] is great as a main meal with [[Vegetables|vegetables]] and [[potatoes]] or with a salad or even as a [[Sandwich|sandwich]] filler.  My favourite way is to have it as a [[Kebab|kebab]]-type filling in [[Pitta bread|pitta bread]] with [[Salad|salad]].\n\nI have included this in the North American recipe category as a homage to the original.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1.3 kg (3 lb) boneless [[Pork shoulder|pork shoulder]].\n| 1 tablespoon coarsely [[Ground black pepper|ground black pepper]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Smoked paprika powder|smoked paprika powder]]\n| 3 tablespoons [[Paprika powder|paprika powder]]\n| 4 tablespoons cane [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Coarse sea salt|coarse sea salt]]\n| 2 teaspoons kona karashi (Japanese [[Mustard powder|mustard powder]])\n| 2 tablespoons [[Garlic powder|garlic powder]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Ginger powder|ginger powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Cayenne pepper|cayenne pepper]] or a [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] mix of your choice\n| &#189; cup  [[Shaoxing rice wine]], [[Sherry|sherry]] or even spirit of your choice\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], peeled and roughly chopped (or equivalent in [[Spring onions|spring onions]] or [[Leeks|leeks]])\n| 1 [[Apple|apple]], peeled, cored and cubed\n\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:The renowned Mr Brown Pulled Pork - Oriental slow roast.jpg|After 4 hours...\nImage:The renowned Mr Brown Pulled Pork - Oriental slow roast marinaded.jpg|Ready to cook\n</gallery>\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 160\u00b0 C (325\u00b0 F - gas 3), [fan oven 140\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Mix the [[Spices|spices]], cut deep slashes all over the meat and rub the mixture well into the pork.\n| Place in a [[Lock & Lock]]-style box and [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] for 24 hours, shaking up now and again.\n| Chop the [[Apple|apple]] and [[Onion|onion]] and place in the base of a [[Baking|baking]] dish\n| Sit the [[Pork|pork]] on top, pour over the [[Wine|wine]] and add a little more rub to the top\n| Cover with [[Tin-foil|tin-foil]] and cook for 4 hours\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nShred with two forks and serve in [[Pitta breads|pitta breads]] with a [[Green salad|green salad]].\n===Chef's notes===\nIf you are not to use it all in one go, only shred what you will use straight away, store the remainder in the [[Refrigerator|refrigerator]], unshredded in a [[Lock & Lock box]]. This way it will stay moist. \nFollow the [[RSPCA Think Pig Checklist]] to make sure that your [[Pork|pork]] has come from pigs that have been reared to higher welfare standards.\n{{Template:See-also-pulled-pork}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:FotoosVanRobin recipes]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#therenownedmrbrownpulledporkoriental #apple #onion #pulledpork #pork #sandwich #pittabreads #wine #coarseseasalt #miseenplace #smokedpaprikapowder </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Thit bo kho Vietnamese beef stew with basil and star-anise) Beef recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#beef #staranise #annattoseeds #ground #onion #newpotatoes #currypowder #shallots #chillies #nuocmam #lemongrass \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Thit bo kho (beef stew with star anise and basil) is a fragrant and spicy Vietnamese beef stew, coloured red from annatto seeds\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2380\n|PortionCalories = 396\n|DatePublished=31st October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 hour 30 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 1 hour 15 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Thit bo kho recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Nice and spicy</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Best with new potatoes!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Vietnamese beef stew with basil and star-anise.jpg|thumb|right|This also went well with [[new potatoes]]!]]\n'''Thit bo kho''' ([[Beef|beef]] [[Stew|stew]] with [[star anise]] and [[Basil|basil]]) is a fragrant and spicy Vietnamese beef stew, coloured red from [[annatto seeds]]. It is a favourite breakfast dish in Vietnam.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 500 g (1.25 lb) lean [[Beef|beef]], cut into bite-sized chinks\n| 2 teaspoons [[annatto seeds]], [[Ground|ground]] to a powder (see chef's note)\n| 2 tablespoons [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]]\n| 3 [[Shallots|shallots]], peeled and chopped\n| 4 [[Fat|fat]] [[Garlic cloves, peeled and crushed|garlic cloves, peeled and crushed]]\n| 2 bird [[Chillies|chillies]], crushed if [[Dried|dried]], chopped if fresh (leave the [[Seeds|seeds]] in if you like it spicy\n| 2 medium sized [[Lemon grass|lemon grass]] stems, bruised to release the aroma\n| 1 tablespoon [[Curry powder|curry powder]]\n| 4 whole [[Star anise|star anise]], [[Dry-roasted|dry-roasted]] and [[Ground|ground]] to a powder in a [[Spice|spice]] grinder or [[Coffee machine|coffee machine]]\n| 700 ml (1.25 [[Pints|pints]]) hot [[Beef|beef]] or [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]]\n| 3 tablespoons [[Nuoc mam|nuoc mam]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[light soy sauce]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Jaggery|jaggery]] or [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]]\n| [[Sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| About 15 chopped [[Basil leaves|basil leaves]], stems removed\n}}\n'''to garnish'''\n* 1 medium [[Onion|onion]], peeled and very thinly sliced\n* Fresh [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]] roughly chopped, stems discarded\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a [[Wok|wok]], add the [[Shallots|shallots]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Chillies|chillies]], [[Annatto powder|annatto powder]], and [[Lemon grass|lemon grass]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] until the [[Onions|onions]] are translucent and the [[Spices|spices]] are releasing their aromas.\n| Add the [[Curry powder|curry powder]] and three quarters of the [[Star anise|star anise]] powder, tip in the [[Beef|beef]] and [[Stir fry|stir fry]] it for a few minutes.\n| Add the [[Stock|stock]], [[Soy sauce|soy sauce]], [[Nuoc mam|nuoc mam]] and the [[Sugar|sugar]].\n| Bring to the [[Boil|boil]], reduce the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 40 minutes to 1 hour by which time the [[Sauce|sauce]] should be reduced a little and the [[Meat|meat]] tender.\n| Add [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] to taste, stir in the remaining [[Star anise|star anise]] powder and the [[Basil leaves|basil leaves]]\n| Serve in bowls garnished with sliced [[Onion|onion]] and [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]]\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Rice|rice]] or fresh [[French bread]]\n===Variations===\nVegetables such as [[carrots]], [[beans]], [[bok choy]] etc can be added if desired.\n===Chef's notes===\nIf you cannot obtain [[Annatto seeds|annatto seeds]], use 2 teaspoons [[Ground|ground]] [[Turmeric powder|turmeric powder]], it will be an acceptable alternative. Coat the [[Beef|beef]] in the [[Turmeric|turmeric]] 10 minutes before [[Browning|browning]] it.\n===Variations===\nThis went well with [[new potatoes]] and would also work well with [[pasta]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Breakfast recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Vietnamese recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#beef #staranise #annattoseeds #ground #onion #newpotatoes #currypowder #shallots #chillies #nuocmam #lemongrass </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }

ginger]], peeled and [[Julienned|julienned]]\n| 5 [[shiitake mushrooms]], thinly sliced\n| 55 g (2 oz) [[Peas|peas]] / [[Beans|beans]] / [[Vegetables|vegetables]] of your choice, [[defrosted]] if [[Frozen|frozen]]\n| 4 teaspoons [[Light soy sauce|light soy sauce]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Shaoxing rice wine]] or [[Dry sherry|dry sherry]]\n| Pinch of [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| Bunch of spring [[Onions|onions]], [[Sliced on the diagonal|sliced on the diagonal]]\n| 85 g (3 oz) [[Pak choy|pak choy]]\n| 85 g (3 oz) [[Beansprouts|beansprouts]]\n| [[Salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| [[Sesame oil]] for garnish\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| If using [[Dried mushrooms|dried mushrooms]], soak in [[Boiled|boiled]] water for 30 minutes first.\n| Cook the [[Noodles|noodles]] as directed on the packet (normally [[Boil|boil]] for 2 to 3 minutes, drain and toss in a little [[Sesame oil|sesame oil]])\n| Heat the [[Groundnut oil|groundnut oil]] in a [[Wok|wok]] over a high heat\n| Add the [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Ginger|ginger]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] until they take a little colour\n| Tip in the [[Mushroom|mushroom]] slices and [[Peas|peas]] or [[Vegetables|vegetables]] of your choice and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] for 3 minutes\n| Add the [[Sherry|sherry]], [[Noodles|noodles]], [[Soy sauce|soy sauce]], [[Sugar|sugar]] and season with [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] - [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] for another minute\n| Add the [[Pak choy|pak choy]] and [[Beansprouts|beansprouts]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] for a minutes or so or until they are done to your liking\n| Arrange on a serving dish and drizzle with [[Sesame oil|sesame oil]]\n}}\n===Variations===\nI prefer to serve the noodles alongside, without mixing with the sauce. I feel it gives a nicer flavour contrast.\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Chow mein]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine|Chow mein]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Chow mein]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Chow mein]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Chow mein]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#noodles #sesameoil #stirfried #beansprouts #peas #vegetablechowmein #garlic #vegetables #pakchoy #ginger #soysauce </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Vegetable nage",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Japanese vegetable nage (stock recipe) \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#vegetablenage #freshherbs #wine #fridge #leek #sieving #staranise #butter #litres #boil #seafood \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Vegetable nage (or Japanese vegetable stock) is very cheap to make and is a great base for many soups and sauces.\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|DatePublished=29th September 2016\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Vegetable nage stock is used in [[Tantan soup with ramen, pak choi and mad eggs]]\n|Servings = 1750ml\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  25 minutes\n|PrepTime =  5 minutes\n|CookTime =  20 minutes\n|TotalCalories = 922\n|PortionCalories = 922\n|Image = [[Image:Tantan soup with ramen, pak choi and mad eggs recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Nice Stock recipe</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.8</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Lovely over noodles.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n===Vegetable nage (or Japanese vegetable stock)===\nThis very cheap and very easy [[Stock|stock]] is a great base for many [[Soups|soups]] and [[Sauces|sauces]]. It makes around 1750ml, which will last for 4 days in the [[Fridge|fridge]] and [[Freeze|freeze]]s very well - we freeze it in 250ml and 500ml containers (most recipes on this site that use it use multiples of these amounts), and also in ice cube [[Freezer|freezer]] bags, so we can pop a couple out for recipes like [[Crab]] Linguine which just uses a little. Making Nage creates one of the most comforting aromas in the world.\n\n''Nage is the term used in the USA for a flavoured liquid used for [[Poaching|poaching]] delicate foods, typically [[Seafood|seafood]]. A traditional nage is a [[Broth|broth]] flavoured with [[White wine|white wine]], [[Vegetables|vegetables]], and [[Herbs|herbs]], in which seafood is [[Poached|poached]]. The liquid is then reduced and thickened with [[Cream|cream]] and/or [[Butter|butter]].'' - Wikipedia\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 3 roughly chopped [[Onions|onions]] \n| 6 chopped [[Carrots|carrots]]\n| 2 chopped [[Celery|celery]] sticks\n| 1 chopped [[Leek|leek]]\n| 2 [[Cloves of garlic|cloves of garlic]] (lightly bashed, optional)\n| 1 quartered [[Lemon|lemon]]\n| \u00bd teaspoon of [[Peppercorns|peppercorns]], pink and/or green ones if you have them, [[Black peppercorns|black peppercorns]] will be fine\n| 1 small [[Bay leaf|bay leaf]]\n| 4 whole [[Star anise|star anise]] (not optional)\n| 2 [[Litres|litres]] of cold water\n| Sprig each of fresh [[Tarragon|tarragon]], [[Basil|basil]], [[Coriander|coriander]], [[Thyme|thyme]] and curly leaf [[Parsley|parsley]]\n| 200ml [[Dry white wine|dry white wine]].\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Put all ingredients except [[Wine|wine]] and [[Fresh herbs|fresh herbs]] in a large pan and bring to the [[Boil|boil]]\n| [[Simmer]] for 10 minutes, then remove from heat\n| Add the [[Fresh herbs|fresh herbs]] and [[Wine|wine]]. Allow to cool\n| It can be sieved and used straight away, but it\u0092s best to leave it in the [[Fridge|fridge]] for 24 hours to let flavours infuse before [[Sieving|sieving]]\n}}\n===Recipe source===\n\n* This recipe comes courtesy of [[Nik and Edwina's Cookbook]], where it is used in their recipe for [[Tantan soup with ramen, pak choi and mad eggs]].\n==See also==\n\n* [[Tantan soup with ramen, pak choi and mad eggs]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes]]\n[[Category:Nik and Edwina's Cookbook recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#vegetablenage #freshherbs #wine #fridge #leek #sieving #staranise #butter #litres #boil #seafood </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Well it was brilliant and did not really need the beef after all.\n[[Image:Very special egg fried rice-ingredients.jpg|300px|thumb|right|Mise en place]]\n\nIt had an almost lemony taste, which I guess was the high amount of [[pickled]] items used.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 350ml cooked and drained [[boiled rice]] from 1 cup of [[basmati rice]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[peanut oil]]\n| 1 [[onion]], peeled and sliced\n| 2 heaped tablespoons finely chopped [[ginger root]] - I used [[Lazy ginger|bottled from the fridge]] as it keeps so well\n| 3 [[cloves garlic, crushed]]\n| &#189; cup [[dried shrimp]], soaked in just [[boiled]] water for 15 minutes, drained and chopped\n| 1 large [[pickled]] [[chili]], chopped, with some seeds and a little [[vinegar]], ''(pictured)''\n| 2 [[pickled]] roast [[red peppers]], chopped with some of the [[vinegar]], ''(pictured)''\n| 2 sun-[[dried]] [[tomatoes]] in [[oil]], chopped, with a little of the oil, ''(pictured)''\n| 4 [[spring onions]], [[chopped on the diagonal]]\n| 2 [[free range eggs]], whisked with 2 teaspoons of [[sesame oil]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[light soy sauce]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[oil]] in a [[wok]] and [[fry]] the [[onion]], [[ginger]] and [[garlic]] on a high heat for 3 minutes\n| Stir in the [[rice]] and mix well\n| Add the chopped [[shrimp]], [[peppers]], [[tomatoes]] and [[chillies]], mix well, reduce the heat and and cook until the [[rice]] is heated.  About 4 minutes if the rice was cold\n| Make a well in the [[rice]] and add the [[egg]] mixture, stir to cook evenly and then mix to distribute\n| Add the [[soy sauce]] and [[spring onions]], stir well and serve\n}}\n===Variations===\n\nFry a little chopped [[bacon]] with the garlic.\n\nTry a little sliced [[Chinese sausage]] instead of the bacon.\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Rice]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine|Rice]]\n[[Category:Egg recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Stir fried]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#veryspecialeggfriedrice #rice #pickled #springonions #tomatoes #vinegar #onion #dried #bacon #garlic #unusualrecipes </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

It was to be a barbecue dish but there is too much good sauce that would be wasted on a barbecue.\n\nThis was an absolute success.  Glad I made detailed notes as this will be repeated. Spicy without being too hot, sweet, without being sickly, fragrant and very tasty.  It's very quick to cook too.  [piggy-pigs - we had this for 2 as prawns were 2 for 1!]\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 medium [[onion]], chopped finely\n| 2 tablespoons of [[ghee]]\n| 400g [[king prawns]], peeled and deveined\n| 1 can of [[coconut milk]]\n}}\n'''Marinade'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1 x 170g can [['Amocan' seasoned shrimp paste]] ([[Sambal Udang Kering]])\n| 2.5 cm fresh [[ginger root]], peeled and [[julienned]]\n| dried [[chillies]], including seeds.\n| 4 or 5 whole star anise 'flowers'\n}}\n'''Garnish'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| Handful of spring onions, chopped\n| Coriander leaves, chopped\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Vietnamese-style spicy prawns coconut.jpg|..after..\nImage:Vietnamese spicy prawns.jpg|Before the coconut milk\nImage:Vietnamese-style spicy prawns in marinade.jpg|Marinading\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| If the [[jaggery]] is hard, soften by adding a little water and microwaving for a few seconds.\n| Mix the marinade ingredients together and whisk so the sugar is dissolved and combined into the marinade.  \n| Add the prawns, stir and refrigerate for 3 or 4 hours if you are able.\n| Heat the [[ghee]] in a wok and fry the onions gently for 5 minutes.  \n| Add the prawns and marinade and heat for 5 minutes, stirring often.  \n| Pour in the [[coconut milk]] and heat for another 5 minutes.  \n|Serve sprinkled with chopped spring onions and coriander leaves.\n}}\n===Serving suggestion===\nServe with [[plain boiled rice]].\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper I agree, Cock Brand curry pastes are very good.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nYellow [[Curry|curry]] ([[Thai]]: &#3649;&#3585;&#3591;&#3585;&#3632;&#3627;&#3619;&#3637;&#3656;, RTGS: [[Kaeng kari|kaeng kari]],  [k&#603;&#720;&#331; kar\u00ec&#720;]; [[Chinese]]: &#40643;&#21654;&#21937;) is one of the more popular [[Curries|curries]] often found in Western Thai restaurants.\n\nMy favourite curry pastes are the [[Cock Brand pastes]].  They go off quickly, even if [[Refrigerated|refrigerated]], but if they are [[Frozen|frozen]], they keep for years.  Even better, you can just remove a few tablespoons of the curry paste even it is frozen.  Brilliant!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 3 tablespoons of yellow [[Curry paste|curry paste]]\n| 400g can of [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]]\n| 450g (1 lb) of [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces.  Breast [[Meat|meat]] is good but I feel the cuts with [[bones]] impart more flavour\n| 3 medium [[Potatoes|potatoes]], peeled and cut into quarters\n| 125g packet of fresh [[Baby sweet corn|baby sweetcorn]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Nam pla|nam pla]] ([[Fish sauce|fish sauce]])\n}}\n'''to garnish'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 30g [[Fried]] [[Onions|onions]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Part [[Boil|boil]] the [[Potatoes|potatoes]] for 7 minutes and set to one side\n| Cut your [[Chicken|chicken]] into bite-sized pieces, cutting through the bone with a cleaver if needed\n| Halve the [[Baby sweetcorn|baby sweetcorn]] cobs\n| Mix the can of [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] well and add to a pan or [[Wok|wok]] together with the yellow [[Curry paste|curry paste]]\n| Add the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces, [[Potatoes|potatoes]], [[Baby sweetcorn|baby sweetcorn]] cobs and [[Nam pla|nam pla]]\n| Bring the [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] to the [[Boil|boil]] and reduce the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 15 minutes\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe garnished with crispy [[Fried|fried]] [[Onions|onions]] on a bed of [[Plain rice|plain rice]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Thai recipes]]\n[[Category:Vietnamese recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#babysweetcorn #coconutmilk #potatoes #chicken #fried #currypaste #onions #nampla #yellowcurry #boil #curry </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Zhajiang mian",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Zhajiang mian, a Chinese recipe Cooking Wiki\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#zhajiangmian #yellowsoybeanpaste #stirfried #yellowbeanpaste #sweetnoodlesauce #noodles #hoisinsauce #pork #springonions #garlic #doubanjiang \n|hashtagrev=12032020\n|description=Zhajiang mian (lit\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n[[Image:Zhajiang mian.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Zhajiang mian]]\n\n'''Zhajiang mian''' (lit. \"fried sauce noodles\") is a northern Chinese dish consisting of thick wheat [[noodles]] topped with a mixture of [[ground]] [[pork]] [[stir fried]] with fermented [[Yellow bean paste|soybean paste]].\n\nIn Beijing cuisine, [[yellow soybean paste]] is used, while in Tianjin and other parts of China [[sweet noodle sauce]], [[hoisin sauce]] , or [[doubanjiang]] may be used in place of the [[yellow soybean paste]]. In the cuisines of Beijing, Tianjin, and northeastern China, the [[Yellow bean paste|soybean paste]] is stir fried and oil is not used.\n\n===Recipe outline===\n* Chop the [[spring onions]] and [[Garlic|garlic]].\n* [[Stir-fry]] the [[minced]] [[pork]] until it is slightly [[brown]]. Remove the [[meat]] from the [[wok]].\n* Stir-fry the [[spring onions]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] until they are slightly brown. (One could also add shredded tofu or soybeans at this stage).\n* Place the meat back into the wok.\n* Add the [[yellow soybean paste]], [[sweet noodle sauce]], [[broad bean paste]], or [[hoisin sauce]] to the mixture with some water and simmer.\n* Serve this meat sauce over [[noodles]]. If desired, add condiments like shredded [[carrots]], shredded [[cucumbers]], [[bean sprouts]], [[scrambled eggs]], fresh [[soybeans]] and hot sauce.\n\nUnlike Korean '''jajangmyeon''', [[cornflour]] is not used to thicken the sauce.\n{{CategoryLine}}\n[[Category:Ingredients]]\n[[Category:Prepared foods]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]]\n{{RecipeSkip}}\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:12032020'>#zhajiangmian #yellowsoybeanpaste #stirfried #yellowbeanpaste #sweetnoodlesauce #noodles #hoisinsauce #pork #springonions #garlic #doubanjiang </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }
